When a discharge from the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are weakened, and cannot be cured by manners of cures; and you see the patient suffering greatly and having strong vigor, then make one great cauterization on the stomach according to what has been spoken here before about the stomach cauterizer, at the circulatory cauterizer; and three subtle cauterizations around the belly, each one a small key, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, make a cauterization on the wrist, and one cauterization on each elbow, and two small cauterizations on the stomach near the great one, for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are ancient and consist of cold and moist corrupted humors, and are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit, then make cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that which is entirely behind beneath the aluminate, a little bit here and there, in a triangular shape, and one cauterization under the belly. Two shall be.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you think that his stomach is chilled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swelling, then one makes a great cauterization on the stomach, as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the mouse at all the key of the cauterizer; and leave the cauterizer open for a long time. After that, cure until he is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the choleritis which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut into the choleritis, heat the cauterizer which seems like a razor, and then put it entirely ablaze on that choleritic cut; and let your hand be there until the cauterizers come to the birth of the vein, so that the blood will not flow; make this once or twice, and if there is much choleritis, then cauterize each one as we have said; after that, cure with ointments that are profitable until they are healed; and if you cauterize a great cauterizer on the navel, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an improperly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot suffer cutting or opening, as we will tell in its place, then comes a disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to someone and is inflamed and discharges putrid matter and corrupted humors, then you must prove the entire tent with great subtlety, and be careful that you know the exact depth of the tent. After that, heat the cauterizer which seems like a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered, and continue the cauterization until those corrupt flesh and humors are burned, once, twice, or thrice, depending on the quantity of what is needed; and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and the great veins. If the fistula goes into the bladder and intestine, then be careful about these places, and do not make any wound except in a charnel house, and think that it is not perilous; after that, cure the patient until he is healed, and if the lesions are sealed and the matters are removed for a long time, then know that the lesion is entirely healed; and if the matters are not removed, know that the lesion is torn and corrupted the bone at its root; and thus as one of those things that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	From the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of cold comes to the kidneys and great windiness, and does not take on a womanly form, then it is necessary that you make a fire cautery on the kidneys from one side and another at the cauterized clave that we have mentioned before; and if we were to cauterize in mid-air, there would be three cauterizations in a line, and they will do more great aid.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a fire cautery on the part outside of the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic area begin, and one to the right and one to the left, each being as long as the length of a foot; and make one cauterization behind the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauterizations be clave-shaped according to the form mentioned earlier.
de la marris	Of the womb
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, and does not allow conception for this reason, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms are late; and when they come, one feels great pain: then it is necessary that one make three cauterizations around the belly, as we have said in the fire cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and let the cauterizations be clave-shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the groin
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the groin of the hainche, and because of this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the joints of the departure are found, then you must cauterize the patient on the groin of the hainche with one cauterization resembling a circle, and sign before the joint around the groin as it turns, so that the groin be inside the circle; and let the cauterizations be such as those which one has cauterized in the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not present, then make three great cauterizations of the olivaire, and let them be as deep as all the layers; and cure it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin of the hainche, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that, you make a cauterization; and the manner of the cauterization is according to two manners: namely, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is according to many manners, one of which is: that you cauterize on the groin of the hainche three triangular cauterizations in this form, and make a good depth and great, and leave between each cauterization the width of a thumb, and be the cauterizations olivaire; sometimes one makes a cauterization in mid-air above the chief of the hainche, because of which there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, then cauterize at the cauterized circle that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the hainche; but make it in this manner so that the circles contain all the hainche, and all the fibers of the layer are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And that is the manner in which one does it in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hainche and does not reach as far as the thigh or leg. And if it reaches as far as the thigh and leg, then make two cauterizations on either side where the patient says that the pain holds them, and one cauterization above the ankle three thumbs to the left; and let the cauterizations be cutellaire, and let the fibers of the layer be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as the toes or almost there, then cauterize where they feel the pain three points or four at the cauterization which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, then make more; and if it is known that the pain is below the kneecap towards the thigh, then make a cauterization at the cutellaire or circular cauterization, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave out so much of the cauterization as to burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do not cause more great annoyance and contraction for the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who have made a cauterization on the ankle of the foot, and left it so that the leg was entirely swollen, and the feet also, and was pierced and corrupted all the toes. After a purge of the belly which led to his death.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a cauterization in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is entirely red and gives off an odor, then put it on the swelling of the wounded thigh, and be turned on the healthy side; and cauterize once .i. cautery again and leave for three days; and then grease with butter, and let the wound remain open a long time; after the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cautery because of the fear of his regard, and if we see one who uses it; and nevertheless these are good cauteries which can be endured by those where it affects.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or percussion or from too great evacuation, or from similar signs of expanded cold matter, none of these likenesses is worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary afterwards that the patient be rid of fetid pills or other similar things, which one makes on the back, there where the pain stays, three lines marked with enche, and in each line five cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and make the cauteries according to the "poins" cautery; and if you see fit, do .iii. cauterizations or .iiii. at the middle hinge of the cautery clamp in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have stiff backs when they rise, and fear; and you find in the lower back and in no other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and it is being cured, then cauterize it with the "celcle" cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery will prick each part of the spine equally. And if you see fit, then cauterize around the spine with the "poignant" cautery .ii. lines or .iii., and let the points be close to one another. After the cure, leave it so long as it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply a cautery in a place of nerve spasms.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of joints is from moistures that are spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which physicians properly call "podagre", and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterization in this manner: make many cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is need to prick on the face of the foot, then make a cautery all over the point that one claims "point". And if the pains come just up to the knee and to other joints, and this happens many times, then make a cautery on each kneecap .iii. cauterizations or .iiii. from each part, all over the olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, then make more, but do not keep your hand there longer than until the sparks of the fire are burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend just to the knee and back, then administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are on the hands, then make points around the wrist .ii. lines; and if there remains pain on the shoulders, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come just to the ribs or just to the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and do good governance to the patient and administer medicines. For if you give him good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the itch of the scalp
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When itch comes in the angles, and the boils descend to the groin and it is newly, then it is necessary that when you see it being cured, he does not move at all that day; and that he uses things which loosen the bowels, so that the wind descends from his belly; after make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath as long as the boils are repaired, and then cauterize at the enche below the itch on the bone of the shoulder, and make a sign like the middle of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with the form that is as follows:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and gives off an odor. Then reset the boils to their place; and have him hold your hand so that they do not return; and work well on the patient's hips, and put a cushion underneath him and a servant above the hips, and another above the breast which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then continue doing so until you reach the bone; and beware subtly that the boil does not burst when you make the cautery; that you do not burn him; and that through this the patient does not die or suffer another harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. It is necessary that the cauterizations of children be subtle according to their measure, and those of great people also great according to theirs; after .iii. days, cure the wound of butter so that the scaling is removed; after apply other ointments until he is healed, and have the patient lie on his back for .xl. days until the wound is well sealed; and it is necessary that his nourishments be stopped long enough, so that the boil does not burst when he gets up to go into chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after .xl. days, when he will want to get up, give him a well-made bandage and wrap it for .xl. more days; and let him have good rest, so that he does not work too much and beware of excessive drinking and eating, and loud shouting; and when he follows this instruction, then he is entirely healed. And I will say hereafter the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the itch of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When itches come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then make one cautery of the same kind according to its quantity, and let the third spark of fire be burned; after cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that one should cauterize at the three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but sign the first one at the starting point and make two lines on either side of the itch, one above it and one below it, and put your hand in the middle of the entire cautery. But the first cauterizations are lighter and more scattered.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to any member, whether from falling or being hurt, and that pain lasts long, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it is necessary for him to be cauterized with the fire called "poins", and the cautery should be done according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, virtue, and location of twists and pain. If he is healed from the first cautery, that's good; if not, start another one on top of it, for such cases are when the member needs to change nearby, so you must make the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of sickness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The illnesses are often helped by fire cautery with great help, and especially the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and do not leave nor remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the entire patient, then make .v. cauteres on the head: one inside the head to nine inches, and the other towards the forehead to the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and leave your hand there until the cauterization reaches the bone, and so that the scales come out and the vapors of the gross humors can issue forth; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it was before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the illness is spread everywhere and it is manifestly dying, then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries on the head, one in front of the neck, and two on the spine of the back, and six on the spine of the back, and one large on the croup and one other below, and two on each shoulder; and two on the flanks, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fossae of the hands; and take care of the nerves that are behind the last vertebra, so you don't burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the elbow, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that when I do more cautery, the more it brings aid and profit; and know that the patient does not feel pain during the cautery as the healthy person feels, because the body is already too corrupted. And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron. Afterward, cure the wound with farina mixed with honey and other cures until he is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any member and is cured by medicines, ointments, and poultices, and it is not healed, then one makes cauteries on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauteries be a little bit inside the hollow of the knee; then cure with unguents until he is healed. And sometimes make a cautery at the hand, foot, or back, at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; and yet no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the art of medicine does not bring any benefit, then one cauterizes with a cautery a little bit deep, according to the quantity of the hollow of the knee, until the discharge is removed, and its color is changed; then cure with farina mixed with dates and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and with blood from colander and almond, each one in equal parts; and mix everything together, and tie it up in a cloth, and apply to the wound as long as he is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of chancres by fire
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When chancres come at the beginning and you see them stop, then cauterize with the fire that seems like a circle, all around the tour of the chancre. And yet wise people say that one should make a cautery also in the middle of the chancre; and yet it does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen some time; and it is more right to cauterize all around, with the fire called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays in dying, either because of the superfluity it makes or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, very old) and he has little blood or because of the time; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize all around with many small cauterizations in a row; afterwards leave it thus. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through the entire cauterization, then heat the cauterization of which this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauterization has pierced the knee, and be such that the patient feels it outside in this manner that the flow of the purging is alleviated. Afterward, cure until he is healed perfectly.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a rotting of the member, for it rots the members just like fire dries out wet logs. If you see this disease in a place that can suffer cautery together with fire, then heat up small and large clavicle cauterizations according to what is necessary at the place where the disease is; afterwards cauterize from all sides until you have removed all the corruption, leaving nothing but what is corrupted. And then leave it for three days, and apply warm oil on the burned places with a poultice, so that the eschars of fire are removed, and all the corruption is gone. Afterwards, cure with unguents bringing forth flesh. If you see after three days that healthy skin does not appear, it's good; and if not, then start again the cautery on what remains of the corrupted places. And this rotting has sometimes been cured by medicine in place of fire cauterization; but nevertheless fire cauterization is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of medicine in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The hairs which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that at the feet because of external causes a disease appears which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a large swelling that hurts the foot. And the treatment for this disease is in two manners. It's to know cautery by fire and hot water. Cautery by fire is when you make one cautery on each toe as if it were a pen nib, and it should be made of good iron to be able to penetrate the nail from all sides and have subtle margins; after that, you put everything hot on the nail, and turn your hand entirely around the nail until it comes to the top of the nail; and then let it sit for three days until it begins to discharge pus; then make a poultice with wild marjoram crushed with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall off and be pulled out from its roots. Then treat the area with ointment, gradually removing flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by external causes within the body, and many times it happens in hands and feet, then it is necessary that you bring hot water cautery; and it is in this manner: take a clay or iron tube, or a pen nib, and place it on the nail and all around, that is to say, hairs growing; and place the tube so that it surrounds everything, then add a little hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the margin of the tube comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water flowing deeply to the root; and let the patient suffer a little from the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will uproot itself entirely from all its roots. Do this again with another one, until you have reached all those within the body, then treat them with ointments which produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cures of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble because of cold or numbness, or quartan fever or other causes, then it is necessary that you make four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one on the belly, and one on the olive-shaped area of the stomach; then let the trembling cease, and hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of foul boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes on the body appear boils or foul pustules that come from corrupted matter. It is necessary at first when they appear to make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made of myrtle wood, so that the point is seized by fire, or of long aristolochia root, or a lenticular cautery. And sometimes one must cauterize them at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further forward, but the superfluous parts from which they come are broken down and healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times it happens that great hemorrhages of blood occur from the artery which is cut at the wound that comes from external causes, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is very grievous to staunch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, if you hasten to place your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and hold them tightly until the blood is calmed under your fingers, and no more flows; then take up to the fire small and large olive-shaped cauterizers, all red ones, as many as there are; then take one, great or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and place it on that vein where you hold your fingers, and hold the cautery so long until the blood is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it starts bleeding again when you lift your fingers off the vein, and the cautery has cooled, then take quickly one other of the cauterizers that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after another until the blood is staunched; and beware that you do not burn the nerve that is below, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, one cannot well staunch it oneself, especially if the artery is large, unless it be by one of the three manners we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding with thread, or by medicines placed on which have the power to staunch blood; and let it be tied and strained correctly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring about staunching by binding tightly with cloth or putting hot things on it, or similar things, if there is no benefit unless a little.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has no mirror or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch well until it is staunched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water frequently so that it is very cold until the blood is frozen and thickened and staunched; and make inquiries ahead about those things which he needs for cauterizers and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the diseases in which it is necessary to make a fire cautery or apply hot medicine, and the wounds, causes, instruments, and forms of cauterizations; and I have placed that chapter from head to foot, and I will go through this chapter by the same way so that one may find more easily what one wishes.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore that I begin this, it is necessary, dear friend, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and for this reason it is necessary to take greater care.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to act foolishly. For many kinds of people come to these cures. Some come with their illness so severe that they will die quickly from the ferocity of their disease, and from the great wickedness of their malady; and one should fear such things.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And among these are those who will give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; but the disease is spiteful. It is not necessary that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but rather place greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly, but wisely about what you are certain of and can take and hold; and use prophecy and indication in the cures of your diseases to which salvation is converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement and droiture, and se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter in discussing by chapters, according to what is before the chapter of cauterizations, which I have described from the beginning to the end, so that you may find more easily those things of which you will have need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full of water from the head
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this sickness often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife holds too tightly the child's head; and sometimes it comes from a cause unknown to us.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this sickness other than in children, and all those that I have seen died; and therefore it seems to me that it is not worth bothering with such treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the head grew bigger each day until it could no longer be borne; and believed so much moisture that he would die, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone above the skull, between the skin and the bone; and the treatment is such when the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you cut into the head a gap wide; and it should also be as long as two nuns, until the moisture runs; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see are the corners of the head opened on each side, and the water jumps forth when you press it with your hand from inside, and this does not come to you: then it is necessary that you cut into the head three cuts according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture outward. Then close the cuts with cloth and powder, and apply vinegar and oil, and leave it so for five days; then release it, and treat the wound by tenting and ointments, and let the head drain evenly, and then feed the patient dry meat of a fat animal with little moisture until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the abscess opens up and the moisture gathers; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes to the right; and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then the place where the abscess opens up and the moisture gathers, and make an incision according to what you are able; and be careful not to cut the artery; and note that there is a flow of blood, so that the patient may die from the bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease called "catarre" in the eyes or at the pit, and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last resort is the cauterization with what will be applied to the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, when you see them coper, that the patient bend his head back; after, he should rub the place with a rough cloth as long as the arteries appear, then extract the patient's neck to the extent of one cloth; then look where the vein bites, and the places on both sides are afterwards the ears, and they are answered; then mark the places with a pin, then cut one and the other with an acut spatula of two parts, as long as the incision comes down to the bone, and it should be by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting in the same way as two do across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood will jump out continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the sense, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space with three fingers, then mark it with a pin and cut up to the bone; and what needs to be done about the blood is that it should flow out in an amount of .vi. c., and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the replenishment of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone point of the skull, cut so that abscesses will not come there, then drain the wound and bind it, and apply ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes, and sharp headache, because of the moistures of tears and heats in temples and old forgotten things and similar cases, and it is treated by methods of medical cures and all that does not help, we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have counted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient bends back his temples' hairs, and feels for the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is little responded except in some men who are too cold; and if it is responded, then extract the patient's neck with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and soak the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which there is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then train it upwards with pincers, and separate well the threads that are below each part; and if the artery is delicate, turn it to the point of the unguent, then cut from that part according to the quantity of two inches. For if it is not cut, blood will not jump out at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And drain the blood of .vi. c., down to .iii.; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a double strong silk thread, so that no bleeding occurs before the wound is sealed, and there will be a flow of blood; then cut off the superfluity that is between the two ties at the same hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize the area with the cutlery knife down to the bone until the arteries are cut; and this is the main work, if the patient does not have a fever and is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization is help to finish the moisture: that's why it is of greater aid to moisters.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the wound with old cotton and puts on well-made tents; and when one removes them, be careful to apply medicines that make flesh grow and tents, until they are healed; and if without any doubt from the artery as long as you work there, hasten to cauterize by fire or employ the leaf of vitriol and strain it in your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you don't have what's present, put a cloth on the wound so that the blood congeals, and raise the wound with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be strained as necessary. And what is most important and lighter in the extraction of arteries is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting into two parts, but the cutting should be well spaced to ward off heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives a space of about an inch, and then when you have signed for cutting into the two joints, and you must use the hot iron on one side as far as the bone, and cut the vein in both joints; and let them be separated between the two shoulders because it is not connected with this cautery from top to bottom; and that's the form of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from the veins that are above the forehead of the chief of the head, and it does not benefit at all from the medicine that is done there, and you see the face of the patient growing red, and feels a buzzing sensation in the forehead as if it were trembling; and thus oil are held tight and moist so that the hairs of the papieras have fallen, and the papieras are scorched by the heat of the tears, therefore this cure is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called it the ancient "cure contuse", and is that you do to the patient who has this disease on their forehead, then make three incisions on the forehead equally spaced according to the length of the forehead; and let one incision be as two fingers wide in the middle of the forehead, going down as far as the nose, and the other two as one finger wide on each side of the papieras, and take care not to cut into the arteries that are on either side of the papieras; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and let each wound be the size of three fingers across in a straight line.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and many cloths to absorb the blood, then put the spatula in two parts where it is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is above the temple up to the second incision; and scrape out all the keratin that is between the two incisions right up to the suture that is on the bone, then do the other side from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then pull back this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	then insert into the first incision the instrument that is called "culterelle", and it is very sharp on one side, and soft on the other side, not at all sharp, and that's the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the sharp edge towards the fatty part of the keratin, and the soft edge towards the bone, and insert it as far as the middle incision. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to what appears from the keratin, and then do the other side in the middle incision up to the other incision; and then extract the blood equally, and express the place where the blood has been taken; then put a tent of old cotton into each incision, and cover with wet cloths soaked in vinegar, oil, and ale, and guard that no abscesses come; and on the third day loosen the stitches, and administer great quantities of lukewarm water, then the ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes' discharge
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes with a great and accustomed cataract, and you see the eyes tight and small, and weakening the sight, and the papieras burned; and the hairs fall out, and the forehead is filled with great pain, and the patient is exhausted; then know by these accidents that those matters and that cataract do not come from a single vein, and the true cure that is there, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And is that you instruct the patient to lift their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead and another one on either side, about a finger's breadth. And start from the temple incision on the left side to the right side, and let it be an incision all the way up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at mealtime; and when the bone is exposed, then stop all the bleeding with a sponge, and then suture between the two lips of the incision and put in old cotton and linen tents; then cover above with wet cloths soaked in vinegar and oil, and take care to prevent abscesses from forming; when it's done, then it's necessary that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then cure with things that make flesh grow.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In the same way: take two parts of wheat flour and three parts of aloes, and make a poultice; and administer it to these wounds in order to promote flesh growth everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the cleaning of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that comes out of the ears is one of the three things: or grains, or beast, or stone or similar thing like iron; or seed, such as jays, beans, peas; or something flowing like water and ale and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When something like a stone or other thing comes out of the ear that doesn't belong there and doesn't grow in the ear, then put the ear in the sun. If you see the stone, distill some violets' oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make it sweat with condiments, and block the nostrils when the sweating comes, and wrap the ear with cloths or wool; and keep the ear above. Many times this cure is effective; and if it's not effective, then administer extraction with subtle pincers, and that's the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it doesn't come out with pincers, that's good; if not, then administer extraction with a fine silk thread; and if it still doesn't come out, then make a chain of lead and insert the head of the chain or the ear canal tightly, and block what is around the chain with soft wax so that the blood cannot enter with the chain; then pull it back firmly, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it still doesn't come out in this way, then take a glue that birds use to make their nests, and put some instrument that is sharp enough for this purpose, and wrap a small piece of cotton around; then press the glue on the stone or whatever it is, and pull it back.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't come out from all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear before an abscess forms and spasms; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient's head bleed, and extract the blood according to its natural virtue, then sit the patient between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat or skin depends; and let the incision be like a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it as far as you can, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a boil that is inside and swells, then administer an extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer one spoonful of gentle remedy according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer an incision of that boil. But do not do this when you think the boil is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with subtle forceps and gentle pressure, as we have said, so that the extraction is easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Then in the ear where water drips into it, it is good for the patient to use condiment first, and fill the ear with old cotton. And let it be placed on that ear itself where the water drips. If it jumps forth because of this, it's fine.
