If not, then take many pieces according to the length you should hold them tight and light, and heat one piece in fire; and put it in the patient's ear, and slide up with another piece from the other side, and strike on another piece on the ear that is in the ear; and do not cease doing this piece by piece until all the water comes out, and thus it will come out entirely; and if you see, then take one reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end into fire until the most thick reed is burned; then redo on the other side of others as many times as the water comes out, just as we have said in the chapter.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an arrow, if it is from a small body, like a sparrow and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is from a large body that can be felt, then administer an extraction with forceps; and it is the thing most easily removed which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of earwigs in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and in the treatise on distillations, and the cure does not help, then it is necessary to look at the ear towards the sun: if there appears any worms, then extract them with subtle forceps; and if none appear, then take the cane of which this form is the shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it should be narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle end in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then suck strongly all the way along the cane; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey to come out, then stop around the cane with cotton as I said in the chapter; and if they do not come out entirely as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proved in the destruction of worms, and you will find it in the treatise on distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, according to the shape which is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of broad silver or bronze below to one small hole, and above to press the distillation with a well-made instrument of bronze for this purpose; and if you see, take a scraper and wrap it around the pointed end with cotton; then pour your oil or juice into it, and what you see of your medicines in the cane, and the cane should be in the ear; then put the scraper inside all the way to the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or comes out of the ear; and the patient will feel it inside, and let the distillation be a little warmed by fire so that you can distill it into the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the stopping up of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a perforation in the ears; and this same thing happens to men by stopping up of wound or birth of some growth inside the ear, and these stoppings come sometimes quite deep into the ear so that one cannot see it; and sometimes happen a little bit further out the perforation, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes quite deep and cannot be seen is of grievous sores in many dispositions, and in that one can see, it is necessary to put the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the opacity apparent, then work with all this instrument according to the shape.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be gentle and cutting before and behind the entire ear, so that it does not hurt the ear; if the opacity is of growth or flesh of the ear, then hold it with subtle forceps and cut lightly, until all that flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the opacity is quite deep in the ear, then take a subtle scraper and lightly heat it by fire, then put it on the flesh of the ear. If you feel the opacity that the patient feels pain to hear, cut lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and powder on vitriol broom; and if you see the ear swelling, then it is necessary that you remove the tent and put in another moist tent made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure him until he is well.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the bleeding comes from the wound, then dip a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are found in the treatise on distillations.
de la char des papieres	On the wax of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	That which comes from the eyes of paper when they are moist and dry, it is necessary that you stretch them with tenacula and forceps, and cut with a spatula made from its roots; then put on the surface vitriol broom.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they shed without shedding, then cauterize with a lenticular subtlety, and the cauterizing after the incision is worth nothing; and many times repair, but no thing remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burned and do not come back.
de la gresle	On the Hellebore
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come from the eyes of paper things that resemble Hellebore in shape and hardness, and because of this is called "Grandine", and it's a gathering of moist substance on the paper above and below; the operation is such: take care if the Grandine moves to one side and then the other, and it's a light thing to know; do then the incision of the wide part, then scrape off each part lightly, then take with forceps, and cut. If you can't cut without piercing a little bit of paper, don't harm the patient; and if the wound is large, assemble it with a seam, and cure until it is healed; and if it's small, don't apply any force, because the ointment will restore it soon and bring forth flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	Et if the stone is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then reverse it and let the stone be pinched, and the edge and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, it does not matter; and when the stone is crushed, then release a stream of salty water, and care for the place where the wound opens up so that the patient becomes well.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is excreted in threads on the papers above, and this happens more often with children than with anyone else, and it bothers them greatly about their eyes, and they come to catharsis at mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush into their eyes; and therefore they lie down on their faces again, and sleep, and are their papers below their eyelids moistened by the exinach which appears in the eye. And when you press the place to your chest and feel the exinach between.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of treatment is that the patient puts their head on your shoulder; and then take one linen cloth, and set up a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach from each part, then put it on them; and press with your chest on both sides, so that the exinach is gathered inside the circle; then make a small incision in the middle of the moist spot, cutting a slit of moderate size, and not larger than the wound one makes when opening a vein; and make the skin firm until you reach the exinach; and in multiple dispositions, the exinach comes out of the incision, according to the shape of a white fatty lump.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take it away in one piece of cloth wrapped between your chest and the outside, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and make sure you do not tear into the incision, or you will reach all the way to the eye and hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the incision, then open up the incision slightly further until it appears; then take it away as we have said, then moisten cloths with oil and water, and put them on the place, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who sweat and put something on top to corrupt the moisture that remains. Then care for it until they are well. And if an abscess comes to the place, then treat it with poultices soothing it until they are well.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on the papers that are not natural and are inflamed, they harm the eyes, and bring forth manners of diseases such as habitual tears and moistening of the papers and albugine, until it is a cause of destruction of the eyes; and there is the cure according to three ways: or by fire cautery together, or by medicinal water according to what is before or in this chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by cauterization, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should put the patient's head on your shoulder, then turn the paper from their eye to your left hand; if it is converted, that's good; if not, take one needle and thread above all; and be this done near the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow near these hairs, and guide the thread above all the paper, and turn it at the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs added, to the entire spot, from the great tear well to small; then take out one thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then sew on top of the paper a figure like that of myrtle, and however it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see the paper is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is someone who needs to cut a great quantity of the paper according to what the paper is moistened; then make on the entire spot above two lines that you have signed, and start from the great tear well to small; and it should be one of the incisions near natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the needle into one of the two corners of the skin, then pull out all the thread; then assemble the two lips with a stitch of a needle to all one piece of fine wool, and stop the bleeding, and make the excess thread stick on both eyelids to any sticky things, if you see doing this; and if not, don't bother, then leave the stitching and threads for three or four days; then care for the wound without stitches or constraining things, because the paper revives at the healing of the wound and its assembly, but the stitching is tedious (as the ancients said), and it is works without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if there is another way: and it is that you sew the paper with a figure like that of myrtle, as we have counted, with three unthreaded needles according to the shape which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what goes over to small equal forces according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are unable to hold the tweezers and the things are not equal, then take a needle with one thread and put it into the figure; and put another thread at the great tear, and the second thread at the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your chest; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have signed, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound with a stitch, and care for it until it is well; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted: then it is necessary to use what we have said about incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of cauterization is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole in it according to what I have said, and then make two cauterizations by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spot are; and cut at the two ends of both parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on what goes over from the paper of the eye, and strain the two cauterizations from both parties together; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and turn black and fall away, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, then apply force, and cure until he is healed; and when the wound is closed, and if the paper is lifted, and they will no longer prickle with hair; and this is the form of the two canines that you will make according to this figure and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works are such that you take a fine needle and insert one thread of soft and subtle silk; then assemble the threads and bind one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then order in the chase another thread of fine silk briefly, and bind the head of the thread; then put the patient's head in your hand; and be in the sun so that the works are declared, for this is a subtle and delicate work; then insert the needle into all the chase along the root of the adjacent hair, and make it pierce through the paper hastily as you pull it out above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and bind that hair in the chase if there is one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs grow forth on all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not grow forth with it, then pull the chase underneath all the thread that you have ordered, until the chase comes forth from below and you see it by the vision of the eye; then pull the chase and the thread, and close the eye and let it rest for two or three days, so that the hair grows back in its place and the flesh is formed above; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural sheep, and be lifted with it or leave it as you please, until it is extended and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the pouring of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or the pouring of oil comes into the eye, it is in two manners: one natural, and the other unnatural. And it occurs suddenly from a wound, or incision, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of the work in it is that you open up this swelling, and separate the lips of it, and put within linens, and tie it so that it becomes healed; and it is not necessary to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict. For if you do this, the disease will return worse than the first one; but you work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and the juice of rose or althea and flax seed be cooked, and ointments of liquid myrrh dissolved in some oil, and wrap it up in a cloth, and treat this way.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you take care to ensure it does not harden in the form it was before; and this work that we have said is nothing other than a remedy for this disease, so that it does not return in the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is below and is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and incision and cautery and similar things; and the way of treatment in it is that you take a needle with two threads, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from left to right until the threads come out on both sides of the flesh; then extract the flesh above the entire needle, and apply force with one spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is necessary, that's good; if not, then take a scraper and put it in the incision, and turn the paper, and make two incisions or cuts inside the paper; and be the edges of the two incisions at the two angles of the incision you have made, and be the angles so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter with no "one Greek"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity of its borders below what ensues from the paper; then join the two severed parts, and sew them together with one thread of linen; then treat this as we have said with softening medicines and cloths, until he is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from incision or seam or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain incision below the hairs of the papers, and according to what has been said before; then sever between the two lips of a cloth, as I have said; and one must do the treatment in accordance with the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare an engine of all their power so that it returns to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary for treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sudden tearing of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling occurs in many cases in a similar manner to the paper above being bound with white of egg, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary that you insert the point of a scraper underneath the paper, and lift it up; and let it be at the pincers, until you cut what is suitable for the fine spatula, which is not too tight nor too loose, so that the patient cannot suffer from the spatula being too tight or damaging the eye; and make your incision, from which you are cutting this assembled thing, slightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and let it be completely healed, and sometimes make a salty water in the eye, and lift up sweet water, and vinegar; then put between the paper and the eye a cloth of linen, and place wet wool on the eye in abundance; and after three days use the colic remedy and similar things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the inflammation of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the inflammation is in two manners: it is nervous and similar to a hard syphilitic ulcer, and another which is not nervous but is similar to white moisture congealed, which when touched with iron and cooked slowly at pincers, one cannot do; and both similarities begin near the great eyelid, and grow little by little until it covers all the sight and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts their head in your lap, then opens their eyes; and lifts the paper to your hand, then coils the inflammation at pincers with small doubleure, and raises it up; then take a needle, and put one hair from a horse, or ox, or cow, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the inflammation, and make it pierce to the entire length of the needle, and tie the inflammation with one thread and raise it up, and scrape off all the hair on the side of the inflammation that follows the prune and silk up to the head, then cut the remaining part at the root of the eyelid to all the fine spatula and small forces; and leave the natural skin or eyelid so that through the incision the body's accustomed tears do not come; and sometimes the inflammation is only on the onion and thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the soft spatula of what it is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the spatula does not touch the fleshy part and break it, and that the prune does not pierce; and after incision, pour a little bit of broom oil into the eye, and make a litargire compound from the celandine, and let it be until the next day; then cure all as needed until he is well.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not numb, and you cannot push the needle in, and the unguents cannot enter, often this appearance of a nail is cured with medicines; and as I have counted in the division, and if you see it covering, then work on the patient's oil and take the spatula slightly firm according to this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And reapply the nail above subtly, and if you see that it does not decrease and the reason approaches quickly, then distill from your mouth into the oil a compound made of litargire, red celandine, and broom oil, and stop the oil until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same act, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the oil, as if an abscess cools down, then apply milk, and first cure the hot abscess until it is well, then resume the work as before, until it is well.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the skin on the wound is harmed in the oil by great harm, then suspend it with an unguent, and cut off a part but not all, so that no more wounds come; then distill into the oil red celandine compound.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the skin that grows on the prune (eyelid)
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Some men's eyes are born with red skin, and it covers the prune (eyelid) and tightens above the papillae and turns towards the back, and appears like a pomegranate rose; and the work is that the patient places his head in your hands, then works on the eyes, and cools all that skin with suitable unguents, and sustains it with force; then cuts off the first skin, and goes on cutting to the razor's edge until the end, and be careful not to bleed the oil at work; and let the incision of the spatula be as we have said in the incision of the nail and in the small forces that one removes the scab, just as the form shows after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is completed and all the skin removed, then apply oil of broom or distill red celandine compound and similar corrosive medicines, and place on the eye a cotton cloth with an egg yolk, so that it becomes sure against hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and blood cools down, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the oil and cure the abscess with soothing things for hot abscess; then return to your work until he is well, and thus make all the skin removed from the eye by this similarity.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you ease the cure of each weak oil by the natural way; and by the accidental way, in iron work; and do not put your hand on any of these works until you see that those members are suffering from this work.
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Scabs are red veins that are covered on the oil, and tolerate with their work and weaken the eyes all the time. It is necessary then at first to look if the oil, in which the scab is, is healthy, and there is no other disease except the scab; then coil it in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head in your hands, then suspend those veins with all the unguent according to its wisdom, and be the unguents subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two unguents by degree in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil the unguents with gentle forces, and remove the blood hour by hour, until you see those veins removed from the oil; and be careful not to bleed the oil at all points of the spatula, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut off more than those veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the oil a green and red compound to corrupt what remains of the scab.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to coil all of that in one hour, then make an embalming on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are soothed and be assured against hot abscess; then resume according to this manner which is before, until he is well; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The doctor names this "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by fire and burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a plan in you that you cut open on the abscess, where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then take it all with the instrument of which this is the form; and it is called "aspre chief", and be made of iron into one sharp point, and be pointed like a razor as it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the surface of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed; and do this some time, then restore the surface with excitative medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is sound, and skin grows, and the body of the bow is sound, and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not heal and is not apostemed, and bad accidents come, know that he is well; if not, then there is no other plan than to bring back the fistula to the neck according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron and burning medicine, and when it is uncovered take one force according to this form, and be the point of iron at three angles, and the rod be softened until the end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the wound, and withdraw your hand from the eye a little, then turn back to the force until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what the veins in his neck do if he holds his hand on his neck; and then restore the surface with dry medicines as I have instructed you, and when the skin grows and hardens the surface, then the matter goes to the neck; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the discharge of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open and do not come from blockage or dimness, it is necessary that you attend to the patient; then bind them with a poultice made of aloe, encens, sarcocolle, and oil, and then strain the eyes; and apply it above with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is this: take soft cloths enough, double each one fourfold, and then place one on top of another according to what the eyes have need of; then strain above with a firm bandage, and begin again with poultices without wounding; then remove the poultices and let the eyes be strained day and night, and if the ligaments soften, it is necessary that you strain them much; then remove the ligament after a day and a night, and if you see the eyes repairing, it is good; if not, begin again with the poultice, cloths, ligament, and poultices until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	rupture of the vitreous humour
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the vitreous humour, then it appears, and comes forth like a grain of resin, and it is unbearable to see; then if you see it covering, the work is such that you put an awl into the root of the part below up to the point above, then put another awl where there is one double thread from the edge of the eyelid; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl according to its position; then cut the loose end of the thread and bind a part of the vitreous humour around, and strain it well, then extract the awl and put on the eye a moist linen cloth in abundance of eggs; and let it be until the threads tie with the vitreous humour, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the vitreous humour each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show great appearance, then pierce them with a subtle spatula that comes in front of the eye, and drain the moisture from the albuginea and descend the eyes, and enter soon after; then strain them until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but the lower part of the eye which is assembled in the eye, resembling a clear water flowing down, and it is not actual water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is this: you make the patient sit on a well-prepared seat and straight-backed, then take the head between your hands from two sides, and gently move it until you see the lower part come up to your eyes; then it will be placed and will not descend and will be restored to its light, and the patient will see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is a clear water, and if the descent of the lower part is not prepared as we have said. Then make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and place it on the corneal tissue one drop at a time by the continuity of the conjunctiva with the corneal tissue and the crown, until the lower part emerges; and when it has emerged, distill hot water mixed with honey or fenugreek into the eye, then be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	tears of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the likenesses of tears in division and what is necessary to pierce; so work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light for the sun, and gently hold the healthy eye and strain it very firmly; then place the paper over the eye on your left hand if the eyes are left, or on your right hand if the eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are right; then place the point of the instrument under the cornea by the thickness of a nail in that spot of the eye at the part of the lesser eyelid, then insert the instrument called "almagda" gently, and turn your hand so it pierces into the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of almagda be at the forefront of the measure of the space which is from the prune to the end of the nose-ring; and this is the crown of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the brightness of the corneal tissue, and then place the instrument just above where the tears are, then press down one path after another. If the tears descend now, the patient will see before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short while, and if the tears rise up again along the second path, put force with the instrument, and when it is placed and does not move, gently extract almagda by rotating your hand little by little; then return to tears with a little bit of silk thread, and leave that in the eye inside. Then put on top of the eye a poultice or moist linen cloth soaked in rose oil and abundance of eggs, and tie it with the healthy eye. We, and those who are of our time, place on top a comb made with an abundance of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some men who have too hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too far in front, but make a subtle pause, then insert almagda as we have said; and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient a bed with soft covers, where he sleeps on his back in a dark room; and be free from all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head or to the right or left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then release him in that same dark house, and test his vision, and make him see some things, and then put the bandage back on up to the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this in the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you delay this, because the tears rise quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If apostemes come again, then you must remove the oil before the seventh day, and direct it towards what soothes the aposteme; and when it is appeased, then remove the sight and put on his face a little ointment to cover it for some days, and remain in that dark house. And then gradually leave the house little by little, and turn back into your own affairs; and know that no disciples should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Irach, who told us that in their land they perform an almagda operation, where they make a cut and let water flow out, but I have never seen any such thing on our earth nor read about it in old books; and by chance this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, because he who does not know them will see; and they are truly made of earth.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of these are of the same subtlety, and the ends in three angles shape.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the knee
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes the flesh on the knee appears to be joined or separated in various ways, because some of them look like scorpions at many joints; and if there are such or it has flesh enchanted with a flux of color, and soft flesh with good color. In that one of these flesh parts which is soft and not enchanted, you must make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the juice onto those flesh parts, and treat them fiercely; then do what you can to support it with a subtle sharp edge from one side, until you know that entire flesh part is completely loosened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be cut off, then work on it with all one of the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if it does not bother you, or the abscess is dead, then follow the sequence as it should be; and if it's malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize as much as the blood is stained and all the flesh parts are loosened, then pour oil or wine on the knee.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the knee works and moisture comes just up to the palace, know that it is healed; and if moisture does not come as it should, know that there is flesh born in the bone above, whereupon the instruments do not come to cut: then you must take one thread of linen a little thick, and be it bound with hands, and have between each night's space one or less; and put the patient's head on the thread in their knee at their power, and treat with odorant as much as it comes through the knee down into the mouth; and many times do this to children at school, and it is a light thing for one who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes through the knee in one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth in the other hand, and know one after another as we are on the thread. Do this until you know that the night has corrupted that flesh, then treat the thread, wipe out the blood, and soak the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back on the knee as before; do this three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of flesh; and then put the knee in a linen cloth for some days until it is healed, and if there is need of dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, whereupon one distills oils and medicines into the knee.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is of silver or earth, resembling an open lamp, like a cask, and lead it thus; and if you see, then make a closed cask, and the instruments be full to purge the head; and have one handle at the head to hold it when one heats the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the knee
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the head of the knee, and grows and becomes great after a while, until it is seen as something to behold; and because of this, you must cut it off at the beginning, and remove all that remains, then put on the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting it off until it is great, then take heed if it is hard, with a flux of color, and poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touchment, not of flux of color, and you see that one can remove all of it, then empty the patient and remove the cutting without fear, and cure the knee with dry and binding things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the knee is cut off and bound
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes to one of these worked cartilages, it profits little, more than in some men. It is necessary then to do what happens to any one, if you look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips to a seam, then cure as much as it is healed; and if the lips are already split from one side to the other, it is necessary that you scrape off all the parts of their keratin until they bleed, then join the two lips to a seam, and strain, and powder with dragon's blood powder, and frankincense powder; and put on the powders a piece of plaster or another plaster binding, and leave it as long as it cures by itself, then cure with oil as much as it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the seam is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we have said in the seam of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men have abscesses inside their lips that are hard, resembling grains of millet, and smaller and larger; then it is necessary to turn the lips, and cut each one open, and take as pincers and cut in each part; then apply the lip after the incision with vinegar powder, until the blood is stopped; and then anoint with oil, and cure the lip with dry things as much as it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a joined flesh grows on the gums that the ancients call "albulus"; then it is necessary that you support it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and let the bow or blood flow; then put vinegar powder or other drying and constricting powders on the wound; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, then cut it off again, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and this is the form of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the ears
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, raw and rough excrescences that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, and green, until corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; then it is necessary that you sit the patient in your hands, and make his eyes be in your sight, and remove the teeth or excrescences as they appear, until there is nothing left; and thus do with the blackness and verdure, and yellowing and other discolorations, until they are purged; and if one removes what is at the first stage, it's good; but if not, then begin again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, because the scraper used to remove teeth has other forms than those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat the tooth with its pain, you should delay pulling it as long as you can, for it must not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance, almost to the point where one has no excuse to regret.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is forced to pull the tooth, it is necessary that you be certain about the aching tooth. Many times did pain afflict the patient, and thought they had found a saint's tooth, and had the good tooth pulled; and yet the pain did not depart because of this, until the bad tooth was extracted, for we have already made this clear to those saints; and when you are well certain about the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scrape all around the tooth with a very fine spatula in order to ward off the gum from all sides; then move it to your hands or with subtle forceps at the first notch and notch, until it is well extracted, then firmly grasp the forceps; and let the patient's jaw be in your saintly grasp between your knees, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out, take one of these instruments and insert it on each side lightly, and then move it as you did before. And if the tooth is pierced and bleeding, it is necessary that you fill it with cloth, where the perforations are; and then strain it subtly with forceps, so that it does not break while being strained; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And do well to watch that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and the patient will return worse than before with greater pains from the root of the first one. And beware that you do not act like ignorant saints who, by their haste and recklessness, break some time the carriage, and do not bring what we have recounted; but sometimes they bring great diseases through the roots that remain, or through the carriage that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the wound with wine, vinegar, and gall; and if bleeding occurs there, which often happens, use the liquid of vitriol to stop it; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, to which one must first bend the teeth, are long points and thick handles, so that they do not double when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick limbs so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of well-forged iron, and have teeth to hold the forceps.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains after pulling, it is necessary that you put a damp cotton ball or two on the wound for one or two days until the wound is softened, then insert the forceps called "algefri", by which the jaw seems to be like a careful nurse; and let them be made inside also like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the entire gum around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is a paline, by which there is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and large so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, it is good; if not, then help with all the instruments, by which the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has two jaws, by which there is the shape:
