et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front of the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like great forceps, by which there is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument should be so strong that it cannot break; and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments that are not counted; and wise master surgeons find for themselves their own instrument, according to what their work and the disease shows them, for there are such diseases where the ancient ones did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of cases; and if one breaks the carriage or some other bones, or it is possible, then one seeks out instruments as I have said, and helps with gestures, by which there is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove; and then restore the wound with medicines suitable for this case, and if there is in the bone a putridity, and it is small, then resect all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural shape in the body, and the form is ugly, and especially in maiden women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly formed after the previous one, and is not in its right place, and cannot be straightened or filed: then cut; and if it is adjacent to the tooth, take this instrument which has the shape, and is similar to a small beak, and be made of well-forged iron with an edge.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file files slowly piece by piece in a few days due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others; and if it appears that one can file it, then use a similar file as this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth slowly piece by piece over a few days, so that it does not move until it takes shape; then smooth it out at the end to any scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and bleeds the tongue, it is necessary to file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth loosen or fall out due to percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press on what they eat without chattering, and you have treated them with restraining medicines, but this does not work; then they need to be restrained by a gold thread, for silver threads become green and putrid, but gold ones never do; and the middle thread should neither be too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are misaligned, take the thread and tie it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the ligatures between the moving teeth, as many as there are or more, until you come to the healthy tooth on the other side; then re-cover the area up to where you started, and strain your hand subtly and gently, until it does not move; and have a secure tie at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then file the ligatures with forceps, assemble them, and re-point them between the healthy teeth, and place them so that they do not hurt the tongue; then leave them thus tight as long as possible, and if they come loose or break, restrain them with another thread; and this will remain and serve thus for all time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy teeth, and the two moving ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	When the tooth falls out, then put it back in its place gradually, piece by piece, as we have said; and do not intervene unless you are a wise and patient person, and sometimes make the shape of a whalebone tooth, and put it back where the defect is, and hold it so as we have said, and it stays and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this ligament comes from under the tongue or is natural, as one is born with it; or by accident of a healed wound; and the works are such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cover the nervous ligament of the large, until the tongue is freed from its dwelling, and if there is hardness or swelling, and it's due to sudden wound, so put an unguent and cover the ligament with a broad one; and be sure that the opening is not too deep for the artery below; and when you have finished, then lift the rose-colored water and ease, or cold water, and place under the tongue a linen tent; and each night, wrap the patient's mouth so the wounds cannot clot. And if bleeding comes, put vitriol powder on the wound; and if the blood flows, cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it is green or black or hard, so the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor and there is moisture, then pour on the unguent, and make a subtle poultice with spathium, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if the blood flows at your operation, put vitriol powder on top until it is stanchied, then return to your operation as long as you are finishing up; then lift the ease and silk water, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes an abscess called "godath" comes inside the throat, which are properly called the two almond-like swellings, and when you cure them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then beware: if it is a hard abscess with small sense and greenish color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, just as for the bleeding of blood; but let it remain until it dies, and then you will divide it, or it would burst on its own; and if it has a whitish color, and the root is subtle, have prepared an instrument to cover it, but first see if the abscesses are calm and appeased. Then make the patient sit before the sun, with their head in your hand, and work the mouth and take hold of the serge between their hands, and press the tongue down onto the entire instrument, so that it takes its shape; and be made of silver or subtle iron, just like small knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And can you press the tongue onto all this instrument and see the abscess, then take the unguent and insert it into the almond-shaped swelling, and draw it upwards as far as you can; and do not touch anything with cloths, then cover it with the instrument, so that it takes its shape, which seems like a force; and yet the head is curved, one side to the other, and are very hard, and is made of iron or lead.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cover it with forceps, so that it takes its shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be torn from one side and the other; and when you have covered one of the almonds, then cover the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and with warm water and ease, and if bleeding comes, gargle the patient with hot water, or grated apple skins that are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stanchied; then cure it as long as it is healed; and sometimes abscesses arise in the throat other than the two almonds, so cover them then in the same way as the two almonds similarly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was born inside her throat, namely one abscess of small sense; and I had well closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the conduit which was obstructed, nor eat or drink, and would have been dead if she remained like this for a day or two. The abscess was so high up that it had already passed through two openings of the mouth. I hastened then, and inserted one unguent into one opening, and drew it forward, and took out a large portion of pus; then refilled the other opening with unguent, and worked on the mouth and pressed the tongue; afterwards I inserted the unguent into this abscess, and covered part of it, and only a little blood flowed out; and thus the conduit of the throat was cleared for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut away at that abscess over a long time; and the abscess recurred repeatedly, and filled up the space I had emptied, until it became very large; afterwards I drained it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it continued to grow; and I left those parts, and only God knew what happened after me.
de l’uve	of the olive oil
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the swelling descends to the olive oil, and it is inflated and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below large and rounded, it is called "olive". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to cover it; and the one that is rounded and assembled, and is not long; and it is sanguine or of red color or black, then it is necessary to eschew the incision on it. For there is great peril above the patient. It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner I have said, to make the patient sit before the sun, and press their tongue onto the instrument that we have made a reminder of here before; then insert the unguent into the olive oil, and draw it down, and cover it with one or two instruments as I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary to not cover more than the superfluous part that is beyond the natural term; for if you cover more, you will cause harm to the voice, and to the word; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it as long as it is healed. And if the patient has fear of covering, then it is necessary to use a trick at the cauterization of the sense with fear. The manner of the cautery is hot water. It is that the patient puts their head in your hand, and then presses their tongue onto the instrument that we have said in the chapter on cautery, and conspires with hot living water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in using this instrument, which takes its shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a head or hair that one applies the medicine to, just as the hives of a beekeeper, and places the instrument on all the medicine above the ulcer; and the patient should lie on their side with their chest open, so that the saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and lungs. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the ulcer for the amount of time equal to half an hour, until you see it is numb and the effects of the medicine are calmed; and if you need, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton in a tube above, until the cotton covers the ulcer; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and wait for three or five days. And if you need to begin the medicine cautery again, then begin it again, and after the cautery, surround the ulcer with cotton wrapped in butter, and cleanse everything around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and cared for gargling until one is well.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, not to mention the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them into one pot, and add oil, and let it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with firm earth, and inside the pot have one instrument made in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it should be made of silver or clay, and one of the keys is inserted into the patient's mouth so that the steam rises to the ulcer through the tube until the ulcer is dead; after that, repeat often until the ulcer dries, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the abscess' heat, for many things happen then; and do not do this except at the decline of the hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put inside it an eggshell, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the steam to weigh on the mouth, and it is good care together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens that there is a lump at the throat or spine of fish or something; so it is necessary to treat what you can see and press the tongue on the sun over all the instrument until you see the thing move; and what does not open up and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing escapes through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or one quarter of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, then pass it through; and when it comes to the light, it will harden, and then pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the top so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the top raised high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglote, lest all go wrong, nor push the bone inside; and move slowly so that the patient puts the instrument in, for it is necessary or the thing to be forced out; then put it down, or pull it out along the entire instrument evenly, until it is completely out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the mucus of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No matter how often the medicine is applied, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient at the sun, after you press the tongue onto the instrument that I told you. And if you see mucus, pull it out slowly with a small hook or fine forceps worth for this purpose. And if this does not work, take a tube made of horn and insert it into the throat of the patient, then put the tip of the tube into the warmth of the tube and do this often. And if the patient is kept in cold water all day, then take a full view of cold water, open the mouth, and spit out without swallowing, and move it to your hand many times; and as soon as the mucus feels the water, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not stop as we have said, then suffumigate the patient with asafoetida at the instrument that I told you in the fumigation of the ulcer; do this many times, for it will cease without trouble. And the manner of the fumigation is that you take a pot with hot coals, and cover it with a perforated cloth in the middle, and in that hole put the keys of the instrument; then pour your fumigation into it, and the patient puts the end of the tube in their mouth, and closes their mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes only to the mucus; and the mucus will now flow, and if it does not flow, then repeat the fumigation many times; and allow the patient to be thirsty, and eat salty things and all, and do not drink water; and thus it is necessary that it flows out by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to remove the mucus is such that when you can see it, it resembles curved forceps for moving into the throat; and has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and has lime-like roughness, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and look at this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what is remembered hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is similar to itself, and that which holds moisture. And the second way is for those that are on the flesh. For abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses of the fatty part are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if abscesses are not to be pierced until the pus is mature according to its completion; and there are some that need to be pierced when they are hard and do not die according to their completion, such as those that occur near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it so long that it becomes putrid around it, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, causing contraction in that member. Or if the abscess is on a principal limb, and you delay perforation until it is matured, it will harm the principal limb; or if it is on the fundament, one should pierce it as soon as it is dead; and one must not pierce an abscess that is hard without digestion being completed, except for those that are near the fundament, lest it become a fistula and be lengthened inside, and thus cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	Et covient que tu saiches l'oure de la perforation de l'aposteme qui est meur selonc l'acomplissement, and that is when the pain is assuaged, and the departements of fever, and the diminishment of pain and heat, and of debate and of setting right the head of the aposteme, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation sit in relation to the aposteme, or more dependent on its place, and where it appears to move; and the perforation be long in the body, and if the apostemes are at hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal or where there is no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that are swollen, according to that member. And when the aposteme is in a charnut place, it's better to leave the perforation until it's confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce before then, the body would be lengthened with venom from him, and full of much filth; and by chance harden the lips and the depths of him. And for any aposteme that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the members need it. It's necessary that you make small perforations in small apostemes, small cuts; and in great apostemes, great cuts, and many fissures according to the appearance of the greatness of the aposteme; and if there are such apostemes where you must sew a seam, and cover; when it becomes as flat as a piece of cloth, and is exhausted, then it's necessary to do as one does with babies: and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such that are covered like the leaf of myrtle, as apostemes of angels; and if there are such where you make a rounded cut, and other cuts and similar covering.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who do not have a head, as if the aposteme is soft and superficial, it's necessary that you pierce thoroughly; and when the aposteme is large, and has coiled great bowels, and you pierce, don't pull out all the bowels in that hour, but pull out one part; then stop the aposteme until the next day, then pull out nothing more above; do this by degrees many times until the bowels come out altogether; likewise if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman bearing, or small children, or old men decrepit. For the hopes sometimes shake with the issue of the bowels, which might cause the patient to die, and you wouldn't notice. Then, therefore, this chapter should be studied with great caution, and when you have pierced your aposteme, stop the wound, and see if the wound from the aposteme is small; and if it's a plain cut, sew tents of linen or old cotton; and if it's a large aposteme, and there are many cuts, it's necessary that you put in each one a tent so they come together against each other; and if you have sewn into the aposteme a part of leather, and wrapped it around, it's necessary that you fill it with old cotton or linen rag without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then remove it, and care for it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs at your work, apply cold and soft linen, and wet one cloth, and place it on the bleeding site by many times. And if the bleeding persists, apply governance and care, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it's in winter, and the sites or apostemes are very nervous, it's necessary that you put up moist tents and cloths in wine and hot oil; and if it's in summer, and the sites are fleshy, it's necessary that you put up moist cloths in water and oil, or cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; then release the aposteme and apply ointment and care, as is necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this should be known universally in the treatments of apostemes: now I have told you how one should proceed with the treatments of apostemes, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Where the cure of the chief comes forth small apostemes, and are manners of ours that are in threads, just as a spider's web; and there are many similarities. Some are fat and such that have moisture like poults; and some are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not make counter. And the work of cutting so is that you test each one with an instrument called "entromissoire", from which the form comes afterwards, whatever it contains. For if it contains moisture, let it be done above the long one. And when the moisture is emptied, scrape off without leaving anything behind the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns again if you leave anything; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and oil, and fill the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will be done to those who remain of the night. And then start the cotton again, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of the night; then cure the wound with ointment as is necessary, until it is healed. And if the aposteme holds a fat night, cut it according to this form, from the long one; and let go your fingerings, and scrape off from all parts, and put all your care in pulling out what lies beneath; and if the artery makes counter, do as I told you afterwards. And similarly do with the aposteme if it is stony, and of cutting and curing as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cut above the stony and moist aposteme is lighter, for they are full of blood. And if there are some of these apostemes or chief that have no moisture, and one of them was an aposteme that I cut on the head of an old woman; and I found the aposteme as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had been made to any, one would have gotten just as much a wound as from a stone. In other apostemes coming from the chief, except those that come from the heads of children and the roots of ears, the opening should always be at the most dependent place, so that the bowels may come out; and care for them as necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these apostemes come at the neck, and below the shoulder blades, and sometimes in the armpits; and some times they come elsewhere on the body, and are many, and are tangled together. And each scrofula is properly inside its own fold, just as the nodule and the aposteme of the head, as we have said; and the likenesses of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that are malignant and do not want to obey health. Therefore, when you see one with good disposition for cutting, and is similar in color to the body, and is quiet on each side, and is not inflamed; and it is not too deep; then it is necessary to cut it above, and scrape off each part, and make the two lips of the wound as fingerings, if you need them, just as we have said in apostemes of the head; and proceed little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and that there is no swelling or trenching, lest your hand escape, and you see too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, so put vitriol or some powder that stops blood in the wound, and bind the wound; and leave it until the abscess is pacified and the wound is softened and begins to rot. And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work until you have completed it; then examine your deed if there are any small scrofulas left, so cut them off and clean them. And if there is a vein in the root of the scrofula that is large, do not need to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread and let it fall without harm; then treat the wound with old Egyptian cotton dipped in oil.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you gather the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no longer any superfluity due to the size of the scrofula. It is necessary that you attend to cutting the root of it, and pulling it forward, and sewing it as we have said. Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, perforate there where it appears moist; and perforate it thus like the one mentioned before, by depending, then apply tenting with oil and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply ointment to promote healing until it is sound.
de squinance	of swelling
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones used to say and talk about the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have swelling, it is necessary that the cut in the throat which is called "epiglote" be avoided; and this is not done by them, because all the veins and the pores of the patient are hot in those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both sides.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the pore, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to escape the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary then, when we wish to cut the epiglote, that we cut it below three circles or four, a small incision across, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the incision of the syphilis, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and they should be suitable for the cutting of the epiglote so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to the entire opening, then cuts the skin as far as it will come to the channel; and avoid letting out blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the syphilis, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the cutting of the phlegm in the channel which jumps forth through the broken place and by the failure of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed about which one doubts strangulation, gather the two lips of the wound of the skin, and sew it all together without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this just yet, until the throat is entirely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the fault is going astray.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut off the epiglote because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and for this reason the ancients command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maiden take one knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut off part of the channels of the pore;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure him, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and saw well that she had not cut any vein or guided it far beyond the throat, and the veins were flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and healed her until she was sound.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it happened to the maiden that she regained her voice, and returned after to her usual condition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in cutting off the epiglote there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of a jasper, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; or natural one has no cunning.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners, one of which resembles fat swelling, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it is not necessary to work hard to make fire except in one who is small, and test and search thoroughly at all the intimate places;
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it just like a small swelling, and cannot be cut by any vein, then cut it off, as one cuts out noses, and treat it throughout its entire head, if there is no blood.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search thoroughly, and cure it as necessary, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of noses
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many kinds of noses are, which I will describe all the likenesses;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I tell all the difference that is between nose and exit.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the exit is hot and feverish, until the ebullition has passed, and the purulence is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the nose there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains a syphilitic abscess, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the flesh, and begins just like a jasper, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two likenesses, or fat, or moist, and very much in color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the nose, that you examine and inquire first by all the instruments which are called "intimate", according to what its form comes or according to the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you take the most moist part that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers and fingers, until you know that the instruments have pierced the kernel, then according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the foreign body, and take care so it does not jump away.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moisture is clear or cloudy, regardless of its color, then proceed as I have said for other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after extracting the foreign body no moisture comes out, know that it is fat, then proceed in a cross shape, and grasp it with pincers, and lightly scrape off each part and keep the skin or flesh intact as you lead it out with the needle.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it apart in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, then the abscess will come back many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a small part remains and the blood troubles you, then apply the wound with some corrosive powders and keep the wound open, and put hot things on the abscess to soothe it, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the abscess is large, then cut off both lips of the wound and cure it with remedies that touch the skin.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein swells up and is contrary to you or another obstacle hinders you, and you are in a hurry, then apply the broken vitriol, and let it remain for two or three days until the wound heals, and stop the bleeding of the blood; then return to the needlework that remains from the thread.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the shapes of foreign bodies, and there are three kinds: great, middle, and small; and among them, there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and among them, there are three kinds: great, middle, and small, in order to encircle abscesses of fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one sews sorceries, and they are made of citrine stone, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are most valuable, and are more proved to be black in order to encircle the abscesses of fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are three kinds: great, middle, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the abscesses.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the probes are many and similar, as you see here: great, middle, and small; and there are also probes that have two abscesses of three kinds.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are also probes that have three abscesses, and they too are of three kinds; and there are also probes that have two abscesses, and probes with only one abscess, and they are all of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The chief of these is to cut, and there are some that do not cut much except from one side, with which one scrapes the abscess, so that one does not touch the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and among these foreign bodies are the threads that are wound around in strips, so that the patient is not aware of the opening of the abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are three kinds: great, small, and middle, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use them much except in certain places such as joints, and arms, and shoulders, and at angles, and in similar places.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling an extractor of fistulas, according to this form, with which one stops the bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is put sometimes in a place where the wound heals by closing the veins and arteries, and sometimes again according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell up when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they seem like women's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must proceed according to this form of the line b up to dot-g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and apply medicine to the wound that touches the skin, then sew together the two lips of the wound with a seam, and cure it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast droops down and is soft because of its size, like it is with women, then make a cut in two places above, through two similar slits.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one end is joined to the other at the end of both, so that the longer line contains the shorter according to this form, from this line b up to line g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and all that is necessary for the cure, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the bleeding of blood, then you must fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive oil.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until the remaining fat and grease are gone, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	I assume this is the title of the section or chapter in the text, which translates to "About Abscesses of Armpits".
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are types of hard scrofulas or those with edges, and among them are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture then need to be cut according to this form, from line b up to line g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with oil suitable for this purpose until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like a scrofula, then do it as we have said in cutting open scrofulas, and if the wound yields pus, then apply fire cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	I assume this is the title of the section or chapter in the text, which translates to "About the Rupture of the Artery".
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above is sewn shut, then many abscesses come forth, and it also happens to the vein that swells up and becomes abscessed.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one recognizes it thus when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep in the front.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it at your fingertips, then you sense one estrangement; and when it is due to the vein, then it seems to be going away in appearance.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cover this abscess and especially when it is under the armpits and around the breasts and in the neck and in many other places and it is very great.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary to apply the iron treatment, and he who is at the head should also apply it, and in him who has an artery swelling above the long skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work on the shape of the scars, and part the artery nicely from the skin, so that it is uncovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then put a needle underneath and make it pierce until the other side, and hold the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then puncture the place between the two strings of an introducer until the liquid that is in it comes out, and loosen the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment as you would to a boil, until the string falls off.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat those with ointment that are suitable for this, until they are healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is for the sake of opening a vein, then it is necessary that you moisten with your hand as much of the abscess as you can to all the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then put the needle underneath the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there be one double thread, so that you draw it out to the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I told you, or join one of the two parts to the two heads of the thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the threads will not come loose, then put another needle underneath all of one thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cover the abscess until the excess fluid comes out, then cover the excess fat of the skin and leave what is tied.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on one damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply treatments with tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses of nerves also come when they are inflamed, or from too great a labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the joints and toes and in all places where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color seems like the color of the flesh, and it occurs in many dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one strains strongly, then the patient feels pain, and it is not in the very depths of the body, but just under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it is swollen on all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor below or above, and the one who has abscesses in joints should not be treated with iron: by chance there would be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who is on the head or forehead, file the skin to the spatula-like.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then hold it with tweezers and cover its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, then suspend it with an awl, and scrape it, then open it up and sew the wound shut along the seam, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of great hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it occurs in bellies and not elsewhere at all, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" by its resemblance to those things, and it has subtle roots and great swellings; and there are small and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw one man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a small root, and were split open, and in them ran a moist fluid.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6, and the work of incision is such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the fungus is white and moist and of a subtle root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	so cut them open with a wide spatula, and the fire cautery is in your presence. For when cutting comes too many great hemorrhages of blood, and if the liquid swells up, then hasten at once to apply the cautery.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient trembling and fearful of the incision with iron, then take one thread well made, and bind the fungus as we have said, and let it be for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then bind it tight, and do not cease to bind the thread of cloth as long as you cut the fungus, and choose by it with great labor; and if the roots are large, then be afraid to cut even more for the belly, but you can well cut half.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not relapse; then treat the wound, and take care that you do not cut the fungus which is of a foul color and poor sense and with a rough look.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an enchanted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of chancres hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the mouth is full
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the mouth comes from the cautery of a wound or a gash of syphilis, and it is on the belly and in some of the bowels, just as it happens in other ulcers, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what has been said before, or from windy humor.
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the ulcer of syphilis and by the discharge of the bowels, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open of diverse discharge.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the discharge of the intestine, then it is even more diverse, and when one presses it with their fingers it will rebound, and then return, and by chance it may be stopped, and greatly increased at the entrance of the bath and from great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is a light thing, and open well when you press it with your hand, not constraining at all; and if it is due to blood, then it appears by these signs as the abscess being large and hard, and fixed according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to windy humor, then it is sensitive to touch, and the work is such that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery, or vein, or windy humor.
