Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	So it is necessary that you leave the treatment alone. For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or bowel, then it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his lower back straight and be stretched out in a straight line, then sign around the belly.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to sit gently between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place you have signed on all the surrounding area,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then extend the top half of the abscess to the great incision;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread or cord made of strong silk tightly, and make sure the knot is secure.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then work on the extended half of the abscess above the ligature, and press your thumb index, and make the intestine move;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught on the ligature, then release it, and push the intestine to the outside of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bowel, take hold of it at the incision, and cut away the superfluity.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery makes you contrary or the vein, go gently around, then come back to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads on them, and insert the two needles around what you have done in a cross shape as if you were piercing it.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then draw the abscess in three layers above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and let the place be as long as it can be, and choose the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is subtle and can be done, then dress the wound as needed, and shape the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then dress the wound as needed, and bind the wound.
dou chancre	of the sore.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division that sores resemble chancre, and how one should work with medicines, and how one should avoid treating with iron; and we say that the sore breaks out in the marshes, and great caution is needed in the treatment, and the ancients say that when a sore is in a place or can be raised like a sore on the breasts, and in the armpits, and in similar places, and one should remove it entirely when it begins; and when it is large and old, then it does not need to be approached, for I never saw anyone recover from it, nor did any doctor before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is in a place or can be removed, as we have said, are that you purge the patient of black bile; then make him sicker if he has manifest repletion; then prepare the patient one good place to do the operation; then throw away your needles or sores, and shape the sore from all parts, and remove it from all parts without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and press well on the wound with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding from the incision of the artery or vein makes you contrary to the operation, then cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then dress the wound with another dressing until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division that the signs of dropsy resemble each other, and how the gathering of water is done, and the signs of each resemblance, and the treatment that is done by medicines, and that which is treated by iron: it is only slight; and one should not touch with iron in these two resemblances: namely, tympanites and yposarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore, when you are treating this resemblance of dropsy called "eclites" with medicines, and the treatment does not help, then look if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as indigestion and similar things; do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient to be of strong virtue, and he only has dropsy without any other disease, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should operate thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	lift the patient upright onto your hands, and have him press his belly by pushing out the water to the lowest part of the stomach, then take the spine according to this shape: And it should be cut into two parts at a point, and yet not so long that it can reach up to the intestine when you put it in, and not hurt it.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look if the dropsy is flowing towards the intestines: if it's necessary, you should cut upwards from the belly .iiij. inches below the navel; and if the dropsy is caused by liver disease, then your incision should be on the left side of the belly .iiij. inches; and if it's due to pleurisy, then it should be on the right side, and it's not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluidities don't flow towards that weak part.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, and push it through, and lift your hand to the entire spine between the skin and the sacrum as if you were shearing like the length of a fingernail or around; then pierce the sacrum until the spine comes out at the eighth vertebra, and that is the place of the water, then treat it freely, and push this instrument which has the form: And it resembles a silver thread, and is made of lead or light clay, and is in the lower part .i. small perforation; and on one side, .iiij. perforations; and .ij. on the other side, and .i. on another; and the ends are cut like a feather, and that is the form of the incision which the writers shape the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	at the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to the water, now descend upon the instrument; empty then half or one third part, for if you empty more than it's necessary in this hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit from the arm, or he falls unconscious, or approaches death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now because of the key which closes the perforation that is on the sacrum, about which I have spoken, so that you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering these things, and draw off a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	do this every day, and take care not to let the water flow so much that there is more than a small amount left. And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave too much water, then his cure will be nothing but a sepulture or sandy grave, and by excessive sweating or bathing and sun exposure, and if he becomes thirsty; and the cure of desiccative medicines should last until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach, liver, and spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	No child is born without a hole in the penis, or the hole is small, or it's not in its place. If this is so, one should soon have it pierced at every interval. One makes a small opening in the pertus and ties it with a cloth, and holds it thus for three days or four, and when it wants to urinate, then the opening is opened, and urine flows, and then it's put back; and by chance, there's no need, because the urine that comes forth neither loosens nor leaves the opening.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose hole is small should be treated with a cloth plug, as we said, and it will expand. Those who do not have the hole in its place are afflicted, because no one is born with the hole at the head of the penis, therefore they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot excrete because the material cannot come out to the edge, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on his back, and then he takes the head of the penis and presses it similarly to the shape of a feather, so that the hole opens up as it should; and take care not to disturb the blood that comes out many times, and if there is any, stop it with what stops blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of boils on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils come on the penis, and it is a foul appearance; and there are some that are malignant and others that are not; therefore you should take them with a subtle poultice, and press and clean all of them, then apply wet cotton in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with divine ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the boil is malignant, with foul color and discharge, it is necessary to apply a cautery. When you have cleaned it out, and the boil is on the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is necessary that you remove the boil that is inside first; and when it is closed up, then cure the one outside. For if you cure them together, the head of the penis will not be certain and may be pierced, and blackness and corruption will come into its place and in the groin; therefore it is necessary to cut out everything that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster made with honey and flour from the rind of green pears and vetch, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if there is bleeding, apply the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauterization is helpful in two dispositions together: that is to say, at the bleeding of blood, and at corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you insert a cloth tube into the penis and have the patient urinate through it; and when the foreskin has been loosened at the head of the penis which has not been circumcised, or it has become so from a wound or abscess, then it is necessary to scrape off with a sharp instrument, until the bond is loosened and the head of the penis is delivered from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	and if this is a grievous thing to do, it is necessary that you scrape off with a small feather some part of the head of the penis and skin; then desist for a while between two, and put on a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water, so that it does not become raw again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the removal of continuity like other wounds; although when we do this work of our own will and properly with children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the most gentle for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not circumcise their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and sages who performed circumcision around a half-inch, with great force, and with all a new knife; it was hot because there are two skins, and by chance if you cut above and leave that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now the recovery is to cut, and it is the double pain, and at the purification of the skin around the wound there is no assurance as to the tip of the member; and at the purification of the flesh by chance the iron escapes and runs the work, and many times they are born thus as if they did not need purification and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification that is done with force to all the fibers I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally well in all parts of the soul's tension; but that the fibers be well stretched around the skin; and the manner of the first operation is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are not doing anything more than simply wrapping the thread around the penis, and then let him enjoy it in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then make him stay between your hands straight and point the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them or any of the instruments; then put your hand on the penis and blow or cut, and pull it up as far as the head of the penis is; then cleanse well the ordure that is assembled there, then tie the wound with a double thread, then tie below one piece to another strand; and hold it with two strings by the second layer at the pouch and the indicated finger, and cut between the two strands, then lift the blade quickly and pull out the head of the penis.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the blood flow slowly and slowly, for it is the mothers; and put powder on top and on top a cloth soaked with a yolk of cooked egg tempered with rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it there until the next day, and cure with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for purification is this: two fingers should be held and should be pressing, and should be the fingers as large as the middle finger equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	the error of purification is when the iron inside bleeds at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you stretch it to your finger, so that the flesh makes an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot keep it at your finger, then hold it with forceps, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it takes three days, and what is below the penis is swollen, then leave it until the abscess is appeased, and scrape it lightly; then cut as you can move, and take care of the part of the penis so that it will not be harmed in any way.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treatment then of the joint of sudden powder wound, as we have said or treated of powders, and if it is coped beyond measure, and it goes up, so it will not harm; treat it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of the urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	Retention of the urine is caused by calcification of stone, or blood frozen, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And if the urine is not released and you see that the retention is due to stone in the urethra or bladder neck, it is necessary for the patient to be bent over his knees; and have his feet placed on the back, and stretch out his belly from above the back, and restrain the patient's anus as much as he can; and then the bladder neck is constrained to express the stone above, by which means the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instruments called "siringue", by which means: and be made of silver subtle and light, like the feathers of a bird; and be 14 inches long and half an inch wide, and be pointed at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take one double thread, and tie a small piece of wool or cotton at the head, and put the head of the thread into the siringue; and cut off the excess thread and stop just at the head of the siringue, then anoint the siringue with oil or butter and hen's egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moistened oil of olive and dry water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then gently put the siringue into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the buttocks; then insert the siringue forward just to the bladder, and let the patient feel come just to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order unless because the guide or sheath is twisted; then pull out all the wool thread and thread, and the urine follows the thread, then draw it forth, and make the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat the siringue until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When fluxes or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled there, and you see distilled waters and medicines, then make all the instrument which is called "clepsedre", and that is the shape:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed and has three perforations: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the holes are shaped so that the medicine comes out in such a way that it stops the penis well without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture and insert when needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you see your medicines going into the bladder, put the head of the kettle in the moisture, and pull on the handle that is there; so pulling the moisture to the kettle, and then push hard on the handle again; and the moisture will go in, and come out now to the bladder, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the shape of the subtle syringe with which one cleanses the bladder: thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or antler, and the handle is higher up; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture you see cleansing the bladder into it, then tie it between two breasts formed by a double thread, and heat one part of that moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the syringe into the penis, then strain your hand on the bladder with all the moisture flowing smoothly, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you don't have the bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle, and punch it around in a circular shape; then put a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle like one assembles a tile, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it into the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, by pressing your hand until the moisture flows to the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stone and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between stone in the kidneys and all the signs, and what kind of stone one should operate on; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder occurs more often in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and it appears hairy, and grates the patient's penis, and it bleeds many times, and then swells up; and many of these stones jump out the foundations; and it is lighter the healing of children until they are three years old, and it is much more grievous in old people, and it occurs in middle-aged men, to those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient by cleansing, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines. For it sometimes hinders finding the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, and turn them upside down and move them below, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes rises up from the high place; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be under his hips, so that the bladder is entirely sloping downward; then search for it and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in its place, then hurry now to cut on top of the stone. And if it doesn't fall when touched all over, then wet your two middle fingers with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child; or your two index fingers, if the patient is young and accomplished; and put them in the foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your fingers, then guide it to the neck of the bladder; then press on top of your fingers, and push it out to the outside where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch out his right hand above to hold the cauls; and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the cauls in the part where one makes the incision; then insert the spatula copant, which has this shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make between those who is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but beside the left side of the navel; and it should be straight above the stone, and your hands should be at the fundament, and be the shape of the traverse so that it is wide enough on the outside, and narrow within, according to the size of the stone, not too great.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance, the pressure if the hands which are at the fundament, will jump away without effort; and know that there is a stone here where it has angles, and margins: thus it is grievous to extract; and there is one that is smooth, resembling a slope, and rounded, from which the issue is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To that stone where it has angles and margins, make the shape larger; and if it does not jump away, then you must extract above the pincers which are like a file at the top, in order to extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you push under one instrument with a curved head; and if you cannot shape it thus, then widen one small hole and if the sand decorticates, then tighten with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there are more than one stone, then push the largest one into the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull it forward, and the small ones afterwards if there are multiple. And if it is very large, then you must make a larger incision. For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out elsewhere so that the wound cannot heal; but nevertheless strive to extract, or to break apart with pincers, as much as you can until you pull it apart piece by piece.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, then dress the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it tight, and put on top one damp cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot aposteme; then resupply the patient above his navel, and do not remove the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, then rise up very well the wound of oil and water, then anoint with diaphrenic ointment and basilicon ointment, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if hot apostemes come to the wound and corrosion, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by that, which is known in such a way that it does not flow with urine: then push your finger into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and destroy it.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound with vinegar and oil of silex, and help him in all ways that you see, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the works that you do to cure him, that you bind his two hips, and assemble the medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and it is in the passage of the penis, and stuck in there, and the urine cannot come out; then cure him as I said before, that you cut it many times, or excuse yourself from cutting because of this cure. I have already tried it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod in the shape and let it be fixed at three angles in one furnace:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then push the rod into the penis gently until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand little by little, as much as you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon after the urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis. Then it will be broken, and jump away with the urine, and the patient will be cured.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this for any reason that hinders it, then tie one thread under the stone and another above, then bend the penis towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it away, and untie the thread, and clean out the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure him until he is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that stones are lodged in women, and if it does happen, then the cure is grievous, and is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that no well-informed woman can be found who will reveal herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a well-informed woman in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone in a woman's body is deeper than in a man's, therefore it is necessary to make a more profound incision, and there is great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessity demands it, then it is necessary that you take a well-informed midwife, and find one who can truly help you, and if you cannot find one, then seek out a subtle and chaste mirror; or present a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command from the examination of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look very well if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary to put her finger on the fundament and seek out the stone; and if she finds it, then force it down under her finger, and command her to push her finger into the wound with the patient, and press her left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until she comes to the root of the hip; then cut above the stone at the root of the hip against the middle of the groin, where it appears more plainly; and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and make the first incision small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then push the rod into the incision, if you feel the stone so far along the wound that the stone can come out forward, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and rounded, and those with ridges; thus know the likenesses to know the issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood overflows, then put vitriol on it and hold it there for an hour until the blood is stanched; then come back to your work, until the stone is out, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the stone from men to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood overflows, and it's from the artery that was cut, then put powder on the wound and strain of tents and bandages, and don't start again with these things, and leave the stone alone, nor pull it out at all, lest perchance the patient would die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of blood is calmed, and the swelling subsides, then return to your work, until the stone is worn out.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Fleshy hernia is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white discharge, which is below the key of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white discharge that we have said; and this does not happen unless there is no.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the origin of this fleshy hernia is weakness that comes to the testicles, and it spreads that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: or it declines to yellowish, or it is without redness, or black, or watery white, and it happens more than that.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this gathering, for if it is white discharge that we have said, then there is a swelling, one long like the shape of an egg, and it does not open up the testicles, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper membrane, then it is a swelling with a part of the egg, and because of this one thinks it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white discharge, then it will be well sensed; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, try to experience it all around the quarter, so that its shape appears as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, then, what comes after the quarter judges what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cut it with iron, then the patient should be cleansed according to our power and the replenishment of their body; then the surgeon sits on their back, on a thing one pace high, and puts many cloths underneath.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on their left side, and command the assistant to sit at the right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the key of the testicles;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula left, and cut through the skin of the testicles from the long side to the finger-like part, and make your incision straight while cutting through the skin of the testicles just up to the white discharge, and scrape it off subtly according to our power.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	then pierce the white discharge thoroughly with an aqueduct to one large perforation, and extract all the water, and then place your fingers and lift up the white discharge upwards; and do not touch the key of the testicles, but only the white discharge itself; cut it out in pieces similarly on both sides, so finely that if you do not cut it well, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the egg jumps away from your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white discharge; then assemble the two leaves of the key of the testicles with a seam, and cure it as you do other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you bind the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the dismemberment of blood; then cut off the testicle to all the suspended parts, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the water is assembled into two parts together, know that they are two hernias; then cut off the other part similarly to what you did with the first one, then stop the bleeding, and put a soft cloth soaked in rose oil on the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another soft cloth soaked in wine and oil on top of the two testicles, and place it above doubled cloths, and tie it with all the strings according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and employ them with carded wool according to this appearance, and let them be assembled by stitching in the girdle of the breeches, and one of the corners takes up to the foundation just to the back, and the other at the finger-like part; and the other chief above the two armpits, and let it be all assembled into a restricted circle within the loop of the breech.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes medicine this hernia with a fire cauterization in place of iron cutting, and it is that you take one subtle cautery cultellaire, and cut through the skin of the testicles, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white discharge containing water is exposed.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	so take the cauter in this form, and pierce that white discharge with your fingers, and scrape it off with this subtle hot cauter.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And cut it in all ways that you can, until you have removed everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and guard against dismemberment of blood, and more so than the works of iron.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing makes you contrariwise, or an abscess forms or dismemberment of blood or anything else, then treat what is making you contrariwise, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is frightened and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, then administer a perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well assured by the signs that we have said that fleshy hernia is laid.
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	so make the patient sit on one high seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below to all the spatula wide, and put the perforation of the long body; and let the holes be large, so that all the water flows away.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound, and tie it, and let the remaining water flow away, then cure it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white cloth does not let the water come out of the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you put a pin or the instrument with which one treats the water of the dropsical, as has been described before; and enlarge one pace the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after 6 months or so, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this hernia there are more fearful conditions, therefore it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and likenesses of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and indeed to the testicles; and it is by many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It's to know that by bitter or hot superfluity, which spreads to the testicles, or from percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the flesh; and it does not find any pain, and it is a grievous abscess
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance there are grievous abscesses that are pale and stony, and of foul color, and sometimes they come from a bruise or an inflamed vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is due to a bruise of an artery, it is known by the warm abscess when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not concern that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	The one who is caused by an inflamed vein is known by its appearance at the expression of feeling with your fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and it can be well done on this appearance and on other limbs;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and you cut the key of the seams, then lift up the swelling and draw out the white ligament, and deliver the suspensory from all parts of the swelling.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the swelling is already bound with these limbs, then it is necessary that you draw out the swelling and cut the ligament.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is in the ligament or in that which is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that tension and cut it again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the limb is behind, then it is necessary that you cut all and draw out the swelling, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is complete, apply the wound with damp wool in rose oil and wine, then care for it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the seams
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a berry, with the softening of the seams.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and if the patient complains greatly when he walks.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment of this disease is just as fearful as the one before.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then bind the suspensory ligament of the seams down to your fingers.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	to all the vessels that are near the groin, and tie them tightly with a thread, and stretch them firmly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then cut at the spatium, making a wide incision through the thickness at the point where the vessels are uncovered.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert an awl where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first location where the vein came in, and tie it again at the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut them straight through, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moistures.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then care for the wound as with others that are opened in this way, so that no vessel is cut that nourishes one of the seams.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by this it does not come to harm, and if all the vessels come to view, then it is necessary to draw out the seams from all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the ligament
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The events of this case are due to the section that comes from the ligament, or the extension above the belly in the part of the inguinal region, therefore the intestines descend from that rupture into one of the seams.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is from the ligament or from its extension, and it comes in these two manners of many causes: either by percussion, or by jump, or by bray, or by lifting a heavy load, and by similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the extension of the ligament are that there is a gradual increase, little by little, over a long time, and it does not come suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal down to the very bottom, because the ligament presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it is from the section of the ligament are that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and there are diverse abscesses appearing underneath the skin close by, and this is because of the issue of the intestine and the body being torn apart from the rupture of the ligament.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the intestine, and are retained in that way, and cause great pain to suffer from the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, therefore one should take precautions.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the operation is that you instruct the patient to insert his hand into the wound and bring out the intestine, if it can be brought in.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then lift it up onto your shoulder between your hands, and raise the hips.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch the skin above, and cut all the skin of the seams from top to bottom.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then bind within the folds of the garment strings according to what you need to open the wound, and make them such that the eyes can issue.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape away the ligament that is underneath the skin of the seams, until the white ligament is completely uncovered from all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	then place your index finger on the seam in which the ligament is located, between the white ligament that is underneath the skin of the swelling and between the second ligament.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and depart that which is behind the swelling, and between the second ligament; then move your hand to the right into the seam of the coils, and lift the white ligament up high on your left hand, and raise the swelling all along the ligament towards the garment.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the attendant to stretch the swelling upwards, and loosen that which is above behind the ligament.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and ask your fingers if there is any part of the intestine wrapped around or white ligament, and if you find anything, then bind it to the belly underneath.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take an awl where there is a thick thread made of 10 threads, and insert it in the back part of the ligament, which is after the skin of the coils, after the garment, then cut off the knots that appear from the threads, as long as there are 4 threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the ligament, which we have said is underneath the skin of the coils, with a strong tie from two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the knots of the threads and bind them together from two parts, so that no vessels that nourish them can enter into them, lest an abscess should not arise.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and place the ligament above so that it is according to the first long ligament two fingerbreadths of that one, and after these two ligaments leave a space of about the thickness of a hen's egg under the key of the scrotum.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after that, shape the other according to the roundness that an egg bears; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the scrotum, until the sac comes out and the bowels, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then anoint with moistened linen in oil, and place on wounds, and I anoint the ligament that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is the white sacrescent part that we have said, after incision, cauterized due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens many times, and leave the ligament until it takes care of itself; and if it does not come out quickly, then warm water is risen, and place on what we have said, until it comes.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is healed perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshly hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this recipe I have never seen anyone dare to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old ones say that it is made in the same way as the recipe that is together with the life, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after cutting above and below lightly.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut in the middle, and treat the abscess of those who work, until the vessels bleed; and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	At no time does hernia come out in the groin, as we have said, and open up the swelling; and none of the intestines go down to the scrotum, and if some do, it is very little, and repair every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and even if it remains too long in this position, the wound or sac will open up until the intestines come out.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens through the extension of the sac which is in the groin, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and inflated the swelling and opens up.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the treatment is by cauterization, as we have said before; and at no time is it cured with iron in this manner.
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and is that the patient lies thus on his back between your hands, then cut the swelling of the hernia inflated to a width according to the quantity of three fingerbreadths.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the sac that is below the skin which surrounds it, then take the right and place it on top of the swelling apparent from the sac.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it to the bottom of the belly, then sew the two swellings apparent from the sac on top of the right and sew one and the other.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the top of the right, and do not cut at all from the sac or stretch the egg any other way, as I have shown you in the treatment of the recipe for the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat it with the treatment of wounds. And when you cut the sons, have the midwife and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sac is constrained, and has no appearance in the hernia, and the cauterization is more fruitful in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum becomes soft in some men, because the contents within are softened, and it is a wonder to behold; and when one wishes to treat it, one must make the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin above the natural skin. Then assemble the two lips into a seam, and if you see fit, sew off the superfluous part of the softened skin at three or four seams. Then cut between the seams, and treat it as other wounds, until it is healed, and the thread falls away.
dou chastrement	of the punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.
