Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that castration is ordained in our law, and because I would like it not to be spoken of in this book, and is only necessary for two ways: one is when the apothecary responds correctly when asked to explain and treat; and the other, because we often need to castrate certain beasts to help us, such as rams and goats and cats and other beasts. I say then that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the one where we do it by attraction, we make the beast sit in warm water until the scrotum are softened and relaxed; then taking hold of them with our hand, until they are remitted and no longer felt. Concerning the castration by cutting: it is necessary that you mark the beast, and press the skin of the scrotum to your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut on each testicle one cut, when you have well circumcised them; and leave a small portion of the sac and the subtle sac which is over the vessels; and this manner of castration is more fruitful than that which is done by attraction, because at attraction something remains of the scrotum, by which the beast desires lust. Then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodite is in two ways in men: one way is that between the two scrotums appears as if it were a figure of a woman's nature, or he has hair and sometimes urinates excessively. And the other manner is in women, who have on their thumb as if it were a male organ and two scrotums. And the treatment for men and women is that you cut off all the excess flesh, and treat it like other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the scrotum, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of tetany
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tetany is a swelling that grows on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to look at; and some women have it just as large as a hand, and this is the treatment. It is necessary that you mark off the superfluity of tetany with your hand or with thorns, and cut it lightly; and do not go too far in cutting, lest bleeding ensue, then treat it with another cure until it is healed; and there is another swelling that arises at the mouth of the marris, and fills up, and by chance bursts forth, and is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease". It is necessary that you cut it, as we have said to treat tetany, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic (or epilepsy)
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratic is when the natural behavior of the woman is not perceived, or if her periods are small; and it is natured by birth or accident due to disease that comes forth; or it is caused by a swelling or subtle sac or esophageal sac, and occurs in the marris, or on the sides, or below, or wherever; and hinders conception, and childbirth, and by chance has no flowers to have; and recognition of this is by the gaze of the bailiff. If the swelling is apparent, it should be done at dawn or dusk. If it is due to subtle sac, and it is near the two lips, you must hasten and thus: put your two fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back, spread out her legs; then have the two lips form, until the subtle sac is removed, and cover the swelling; then take linen, moisten it in oil, and place it on the swelling, and have the woman rest at home each day, so that she cannot move. And if the swelling is hard and esophageal, you must cut it off like a mulberry leaf. If the swelling is of natural flesh, you must suspend it with thorns and cut it; and use medicines to stay blood, such as aconite, dragon's blood, incense, and in combination with egg-white; then administer a bandage of cloth, so that the wound cannot close; and thus be long-lasting, and administer a tent of linen to dry; then be cured by other cures until it is healed. And when flesh comes forth from the marris, you must cut it according to this manner, unless it is enchanted apostemes. For an enchanted aposteme in the marris should not be touched with fire.
des emorroides	from hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins without any normal covering, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thrombosed; and we have said in the division the likenesses of these things, and their signs, and I will say here those that can be cured.
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses of the thigh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	abscesses of the thigh come in many manners, such as chancre and boilous abscess and herpes and ulcers and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division. It is necessary then that I speak about the hot abscess that comes to the thigh, which is not one of the abscesses that surround a bow; and if you wish to know how to work with iron, look first whether the abscess is swollen at the beginning of its onset, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red and you can see it. Then do not hasten to pierce, but let it subside as long as the pain subsides; and then have the patient sit on one seat, with two small seats or he leans, and support him on his back and assemble his feet to the parts behind the leg; and be his groins expanded, and put his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good bandage; then place the ball of the thigh towards the right costal area, and administer the instrument for working the mouth of the thigh, from which comes the form; and it is necessary that when you administer this instrument, you insert the first rate to know the depth of the thigh, so that what enters into the instrument does not come further in than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, one must cover the depth of the thigh with cloths, so that the instrument does not grieve; and it is necessary that he places the horn of the instrument above, and holds the instrument. And when the abscess opens, and one works on it gently by hand, then it is necessary to close it at the head, at the spatula-like let; and when the bow is empty, then it is necessary to put into the wound moistened tents in rose oil or green oil; and place the tent away from the wound at the depth of the thigh, and place behind the thigh and on the pointed linen cloth, well moistened with water or herbs cooked; then cure after two days' ointment, as it is fitting, until it is healed; and sometimes one opens the thigh and the wound by a syringe of water and honey, and then by water or roots of lily and aristologe long cooked; then return to ointment. And if the wound is reopened in the thigh, it is necessary that you take care not to work with iron, but cure as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary first to know the figure of natural childbirth and its signs, when you see the woman hastening downward, and desiring to give birth; then the child hastens to issue forth; then you know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue is below the crown, and the secondine with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly, so that the child may issue quickly; for when it descends above the crown, the secondine follows with it, and the marris are relieved of its superfluities by good purging; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes between her feet, or above the body or hands, or on her belly, or in some other way, and is converted by chance to the back, and by other evil figures; therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should aid her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes forth above its head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her virtues are weak, then have her sit on a stool or that women hold her; and have her nature be anointed with oil or fenugreek cooked, and then pour the balm between her breasts, little spatula-like in form.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and split the secondine, and cut to its length as long as the moistors that are in it flow; and press on the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to catheterize the woman with fenugreek and sesame oil mixture; then have her press and stretch with conditions, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the child has issued. And if the two hands come forth, it is necessary that you gently pull them out piece by piece; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet up; then remove the seat from the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child has died, then cut off the hands at the knife that was placed before, and extract the child, and pull it out evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	the issue of the child between its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes out between its feet, it is necessary to pull it up.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it piece by piece until it is even.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one of the feet and stretch it piece by piece.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	until it reaches the groin, then instruct her to press, and have her stretch with conditions.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	and jump forth, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not forth as we have said, then turn it piece by piece until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it comes forth easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take musk-scented powder and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind all together in one mortar.
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put it on the woman's nature, inside and outside this balm.
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then have her sit in hot water down to the navel.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened below, have her take a mercury collar and put it on underneath, and leave it for an hour.
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then have her sit on a stool, then have her stretch and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press on her belly, for the child is now jumping.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	the issue of the child between its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes forth in this form, then put the balm on its hands piece by piece.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then be placed on its back, with its feet hanging down below, and be laid on a bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold its hands piece by piece, and then press its hands on the belly, and remove the cushions underneath until it is prepared to go down.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, then take its feet and shape them properly, then shape the belly upwards, then insert your hands.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and pull out the child piece by piece; and instruct the woman to take hold of it until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child which comes forth from the womb with one hand during labor.
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to contrive to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If one cannot bring it back, then let the woman get up and walk;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then let her lie on one bed, and lift up her legs properly;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the poultice which I have recounted;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not deliver, then let her sit on one stool, and then strive to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and follow the child according to its natural form, and make it cry out, and instruct her to grasp as long as the afterbirth issues forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child from its mother's neck, and have its hands spread out, and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the nurse takes hold of the hand, then turns it slightly and gently.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, then applies the natural poultice of oil and ointment, as we have said, and instructs her to move it slightly.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, then let her sit on one stool, and instruct her to grasp; and make it cry out.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner for the entire afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes forth in this way with all the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth at your finger's length, until the moisture is drained.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child stretches out its face and neck, then cut from the mouth so that it is not retained, and let the child die.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child in, as long as you have placed it so that it is necessary, and instruct the woman to grasp sometimes:
adonques si istra legierement.	then it comes forth lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not an uncommon thing, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a rare thing, and do not live unless one name applies;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and are deprived by the placenta which divides them, which is tied to the mouth;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they issue naturally as one child does, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they issue grievously, then follow the cure as we have said, and be a subtle nurse, and do quickly and lightly what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it is of value for their salvation.
de plusors enfans	of multiple children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or more up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of an infant by the measurement of God's glory,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary that the nurse knows all this, for sometimes similar things happen to her.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you are treating a woman for a dead child or afterbirth, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are constrained to use force of hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know whether the woman is of sound virtue and has no accident or does not fear death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be stooping forward on her back, and have her knees bent down, and her legs lifted;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the servant takes hold of her by two parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not treated on the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then anoint the mouth of the afterbirth with moist oils mixed with the poultice of althea and fenugreek and flaxseed, then grease the nurse's hands with these oils and poultices.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then put them into the afterbirth lightly, then take one or two leeches that are suitable for this purpose,
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and beware if the child is prepared to descend upon its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	so place the leeches in his eyes, or on his neck, or in his mouth, or on his palate, or under the beard, or in the navel, or near the ribs;
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is on the feet, then place or prick them and make the edges of the skin moles.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that you hold the leech in your right hand, and put the hook between the two fingers of your left hand, and anoint all his hand lightly, and place the leech on any one of those places which we have said, until it comes to the empty place.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the leech;
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then place another leech opposite it, or a third one if you need it, so that the extractions are equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch them equally by moving from one side to the other, so that the extractions may come out, and let the leeches be teeth-like to hold in place, as is its form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if one part remains, then anoint the nurse with some oil on his fingers, and put them in that part, and treat the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there is none left, then put this leech or more high up, and do so until all comes forth fully.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back due to constriction,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then it is necessary that you wrap it in a cloth, until it comes out completely;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then cut at the joint of the toe or at the ankle, and do so in the other hand, and with two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's head is large and it is narrow in the issue, or has an aquiline nose assembled;
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	then it is necessary that you put the spatula-like spine between your fingers, and shape the head and extract the aquiline nose;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you will round it at the instrument which is called "almidach", from which comes the form with the instruments or chapter that follows this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and do thus naturally so if the child has a great natural head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then treat the bones with pincers,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head jumps forth and it is strained to the navel, then be split open, until the moisture that is in the afterbirth comes forth.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then it is necessary that you make a hole until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the attraction is gentle, and the directions to the mouth of the marriage are gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is swollen in the belly or breast, then you must extract it with one wrap of cloth wrapped around your hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and make an incision in the belly or breast, as long as the moisture that is there persists.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other limbs are broken, and the head remains.
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	so that the barber puts his hand into the very depth of the marriage, and draws it just to the mouth of the marriage.
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then he puts one or two threads on it, and pulls it further.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the marriage is narrowed because of a hot abscess that has come there, then it is not necessary to work on it.
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	rather it is necessary to administer things moist and greasy.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and the administrator applies ointments, and gives in water that is softening and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side and you can put it equal, then administer what we have said to the living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one cannot do this, then draw it further by parts, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, administer what we have said to abscesses that come in the marriage.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if bloody discharges come, it should be put in water restraining, and administer other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman who had a child dead in her womb, then she consulted one other on that child and brought the dead child to life again.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time an abscess came in her belly and swelled so much that it opened up, and began to cause great turmoil.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned for the treatment, and I thought for a long time, and could not stop the wound from bleeding.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on an ointment of strong attraction, and one bone came out, and after some days another did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I cleaned the wound and pulled out many bones until the woman was in better condition;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived for a long time like this, and every now and then a piece of flesh would fall off.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have not forgotten this chapter except that when the master finds a strange thing, he knows how to put aid there.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	about bringing the marriage back to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the presbyter, to which we give books; and to two turnings at two joints of two lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the combs should be more subtle than the restrainer, and should be made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the fist should be one and a half palms wide, and the edges of the trees one palm, and from long a palm and a half;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two lines there should be two joinings of this same fist, which should be fixed in one and the other, a half palm long or a little more.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two joinings are inserted in the mouth of the marriage so that it can open when one turns the two combs.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, with its appearance more subtle and lighter, should be made of fist-shaped ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of pincers.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have at two joints two joinings, just as you see, one palm long and one and a half palms wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see the marriage open with all the instrument, then make the woman sit on one bed, her feet stretched out and her legs apart.
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then put the two joinings joined together in the marriage, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand on the whole instrument, just as you have done with pincers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the marriage, until the barber does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted and multiplied in their forms; and when the mirrors have prepared them, the work is then more hasty and higher among men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	So do not despise the instrument that you have prepared, because their needs are not at all excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained at childbirth, then you must instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then make her exhale slowly, and hold your hands on the mouth and navel.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she starts because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, then take one pot, and make a hole or cover, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marriage, such as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, cassialine, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put one end of the pot or hole and the other end into the mouth of the marriage.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let it stay until the vapors come inside the marriage; then make her exhale, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine starts hastily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if she remains after this treatment and is not fully cured, then instruct the barber to wet her left hand with sesame oil or muskallage of alethe, and then put it in its natural state.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and if the secondine wants it; and when she has found it, then take hold of it and stretch it a little bit at a time straightly, so that the marriage does not become dislocated during the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it should be moved slightly to the right and left, and then pulled; and it will come out and become dislodged.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the marriage is narrowed, as we have said, the cure is to exhale and perform a fumigation with herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she is not cured by all that we have said, then beware that you do not force it to come out.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but what is at the mouth of the marriage, you must tie it to the woman's thigh, then anoint her with oil of tetra-pharmaceutical ointment.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	so it will bring her relief and recovery, and come forth; but nevertheless, when she has passed this stage, a bad odor will come up to the stomach and head, and harm the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary to make suitable fumigations for this: some of the ancients have experimented with the fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument by which one fumigates the woman to retain flowers and secondines is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it resembles seeing a chain, and one places the thin head in nature, and the wide handles above the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and the fumigation is above the coals, and the woman is treated until she is exhausted, and another one begins again.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but rather it is stopped by a subtle abscess:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore it is necessary for the doctor to pierce that abscess at its root, and not to pierce too sharply or suddenly, and be careful not to touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply a moist linen in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop, put a thread of linen cloth through and let it stay for several days, and then remove it when the child wants to go to the chamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this abscess comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess; therefore it is necessary to cover that sudden abscess: if it be cured, as we have said about the linen thread.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodulation, and grow bigger than those that come from beside the foundation or in the space of two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodulation is old, it works, and brings forth moisture in white or subtle blood.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas burst open; and they are known by this that there is emission or ejection or ventosity when the patient makes an emission, and by chance one jumps out suddenly.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis; and they reach just to the joint of the thigh, and just to nothing of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the fistula bursting at the foundation, and not bursting:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you push your index finger or foundation, and push in a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has tortuosity, then I push in a thin thread of linen or one hair of a horse, as far as you feel the thread or hair at your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no emission or ventosity or pus, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not pierce; then hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula bursts just to the bladder or just to the urethral conduit of urine, then the urine jumps out, and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced just to the joint of the thigh, then the thread comes out just to the level;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain around it, then it is that it comes out again with blood, and it does not help by medicine or by gentle application with ointment.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these burst-open fistulas there is no cure other than labor, and the vanity of foolish mirrors that meddle with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In those that are not burst-open and are not old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experimented.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lifts up his legs until they are above his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then push in a thread of iron or linen if there is tortuosity, as far as you know where the thread comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the foundation, then it is necessary that you push in your index finger.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	if it feels then that the thread has pierced it; and be discovered where you feel between your finger and the abscess or flesh, then know that it is burst.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	so one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is said that some can be healed, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help one gives is that one cauterizes the subtle fire according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and push it all hot into the fistula, as far as it comes to the foundation; and do this two or three times, until you know that these charred things are burned, which are similar to a bird's feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat with moist threads in butter, until those charred things are gone; and then treat with ointment anointing the wound and closing it.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If he is thus healed, that's good. If not, there is no other way to heal him.
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the thread goes in and does not pierce just to the level of the foundation, and there is a thick covering between your finger and the thread of flesh or abscess, and you see the fistula at the place where the covering ends from the heat.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	then cut at the beginning of the fistula, and push in ahead of the thread, and then apply the cauter after, as far as it comes to the top of the thread.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the thread will be delivered and fall; then scrape off those charred things that resemble a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood flows forth, and comes between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicinal agent quickly.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cauterizes two things: that is to say, the burning of these charred things, and the drying up of blood and the scorching of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then treat with moist threads in butter or mixed broth, as long as the wound weeps blood, and the charred things are gone from the wound.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound with ointments that close and seal hard flesh, and the medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes just to the very foundation and is separated from the body, then push your index finger or foundation in and investigate this.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the thread and there are two of them, one is the cloth or abscess or char, which is very close to piercing, if there are no forces except for the way of faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	You burn it as we have said, or you cut to the bone, or if you can, put tents and care for it as first.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too far into the depth, lest you cut through the tent that holds the foundation, and the evacuations will come about without your intention.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then care for it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance if it will be clean, or you remove that covering and wash it when it is cut beneath the foundation, or by tent or other appointed instrument.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then cleanse the sore flesh that is in the wound, as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound and to keep the fistula in the part beyond the foundation: if it were a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas are thus: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the foundation near the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if you take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put one twisted thread into two, and put the tent all over the thread in the fistula as far as the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced on the edge of the foundation within, then draw out the thread from that puncture, so that you put your two or foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and pull the top of the thread, and bring together the two ends, and hold one to another, and leave it for one day or two.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and hold it sometimes, until the threads cut through those flesh parts that are between them, and break.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then care for the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, then make it open in all ways that you can, unless it is too far down.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to cut through the tightening so deep, and then care for it, as we have said, until it is clean.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spine-like spinous bone from which one makes the fistula is much rougher at one end and cut off.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not, therefore one does not cut there what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of ulcers
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Ulcers are according to two manners: or they are within the foundation, like a kernel of resin, and there are small and great ones, and in short time blood flows.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and in short time or a little bit of yellow water or a little bit of blood comes out, and they have the color of flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the care for those who have them within the foundation is that you instruct the patient to sit on a stool or chair, until the foundation comes forth, and the threads appear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and hold it with pincers or at your finger, then cut it at its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the ligaments cannot hold them due to their moisture, then take them on one cloth or cotton or a piece of camlet.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and draw them out to your two hands, then cut them, and powder with some hot powders that are in place of cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you burn them as it is said or written in the chapter on cautery, then care for them with other cares until he is healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot come out, then purge the patient with a bitter and harsh purgative to wash what is in the foundation, so that it can come out clearly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient is prepared, and if the threads are above the foundation, then the care is light.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them at your finger or with pincers, and cut them, then care for them as we have said, until he is healed, and so that he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you bring the suture in this manner: take one twisted thread, and put it into a needle, and then pull the thread up and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is of the size; and hold the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and draw out the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one for correcting the excess blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put a moist cloth on the foundation in rose oil or cerate, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave him until they bleed, and when they have stopped bleeding, then care for them with ointment and other care, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the wound of the devil or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times it happens that a wound appears in the intestine, and by natural constraint, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you scrape off the skin above at the point of a spine or at your finger, which does not let it moisten.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then care for it until it is closed as it should be.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot close, then repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until it is healed and scraped.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then care for it until he is healed.
dou fremit	of the tremor
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formic is a small, foul-smelling appearance above the skin, and goes deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it turns the flesh cold, and one feels it just like a person dying of tremor, and comes to all the skin, and more on the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the care is that you take a cord from an ostrich feather or a strong goose's feather, and put that cord on the tremor, until the circles mark out the tremor all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand around the whole cord until you cut all around the tremor, and put it deep, and extract the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, then do this with a cord of iron or steel in this form, and be subtle below and pulling up above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, but hold it to the two and press it And if you see, then burn the tremor, as is written before or in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the purgative
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a purgative of silver or archite, or melted iron or cloth; and sometimes one makes these small and large instruments according to the way they are brought together.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those to be treated with care in the cure of children and those who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of a colostomy is both small and great if it is above wide; or the bellies are tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has an obstruction or the bellies are tied, as you see, and the head is pierced from within; and has two holes on one side and one on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and it is tied or the bellies are wrapped with medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and has between each hole one span of space, then put into these holes one strong thread twisted in ten or eleven times around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie it with an instrument in front of a strong thread, then colostomize; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the colostomy with oil or egg yolk or similar thing, then bind it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then press the ministers with his two hands together until it is all visible, then extract the colostomy, and lift the patient's legs to the appearance.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, then tie it as tight as you can; and if he sleeps for an entire night, then it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you colostomize him in the disease of bowel obstruction, and the medicine hastens to come out, then continue it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if hemorrhoids are on the fundament or abscess, then make the colostomy just as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle colostomy when the skin is stretched tight.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell the treatments by hand and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by cutting with stone, or the edge of a sword and knife, or a lance or club or stick, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or those that are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and begin with the wounds of the head that are simple, for the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is from cutting with stone or similar things, and the skin is altogether torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt slightly about abscesses hot: if you make it heal quickly with the head's own medicine itself, even if it comes out with blood from the wound, and let the healing go against the injured part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and instruct the patient to take repletion of wine and large meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he doesn't want to heal, then diminish his meat and not drink wine or eat flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come, a moist cloth soaked in rose oil or wine alone.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh and still full of blood, and has not been affected by air or powder, which I will say a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the air has changed it, then put on some ointments until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a cut with a sword and similar things, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together by suturing, just as I will say about wounds of the belly, in the chapter on suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is open to the bone and pours, and holds on only by a little, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as cooked testicles and wheat, also like pigeons, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or skin rotting, and it is not at the bone, then cut out all the rotten part and clean it, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if he has an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be stopped without cutting, and it cannot be stayed by medicine, then cut the artery, and if you find it severed, then tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you put in this powder which solidifies even when air has changed it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is this: take equal parts of incense and blood of dragon; three parts of live coal; and mix the powder finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and fill the wound, and bind it firmly, until it closes well and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and let it remain unbound, unless it swells; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one never does this with coal alone, unless one has neither incense nor blood of dragon, but only when the air has changed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the air has changed the wound, even if it is fresh, then one must not put in this powder.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive ointments, or pigeons made of wheat flour, water, and honey, until it overflows.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a bone break comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there being no difference between it and one of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or an artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerves, then there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and not put anything restraining, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substances of nurses are cold, and their continuity is with the brain, which is the highest member
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but make the medication thick, like chalk washed in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and wash the cloth also in sweet water,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones from mines according to this manner, and oily unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up with threads, then apply a dressing until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and the flesh is broken and full of pus, then pierce or open it lower down;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and bleeding comes from it, then bind it, and tie it, and cauterize as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the windpipe of the throat is cut or the gullets, and the ducts are kept, by which the flesh goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	then sew up the gullet on the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then strain it gently, and leave it for some days, then treat it with dry ointments until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then scrape it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are fragments of bone, then remove all that you can, and leave what you cannot take out until the wound has healed.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and then loosen and open the abscess.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound caused by a lance or sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or sword and the wound is deep, then look to see if there are signs of gangrene coming from the wound and the patient is going to die: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put powder on it at the first hour nor bind it for the blood that does not congeal deeply.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and returns to the heart, and kills the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but put attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to absorb excess moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if it does not come with convulsion, nor bad trembling of the heart, nor any sign of death.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good dispositions, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure it with tents and other treatments, until it is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and he works, then know that there is a fistula; then treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a cut by sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse, on the back, then treat it as one would for those in front.
