s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone and has broken pieces, then scrape the wound, and remove the fragments that are loose.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not loose, then leave the wound to heal, and loosen the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the great wound, sometimes the intestines burst open or the intestines themselves, by which the introduction of contents;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse than a small wound to treat a large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	therefore one should put the intestines back in slowly, not all at once.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell at once when they feel cold, and then enter more slowly.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and therefore it is better to treat the medium wound, because one should return the intestine to its place just like with others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to three manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common stitches happen in the stitching of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitch for other wounds on the body and the two other stitches that are proper are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and all the same they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine protrudes out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if a thing must be put back, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said.
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or one cloth in lukewarm water only.
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook in water of aqua composita, and cypress, and spike.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and apply the intestine until the swelling is removed.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes it makes the wine restraining, and it becomes wet that it only serves to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, then moisten the intestine with water or broth that has been cooked with marshmallow and melicote.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because of this, the entrance is loosened to a small extent.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a little hole in the wound with the instrument used to lance hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is more important than the cut,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	unless there is great necessity for it.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	then cut inside the curvature and do not go too far, and look at the shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine protrudes out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back in its natural shape to its proper place.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you can manage it, for this is more important.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large and it is in the lower part of the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part of the belly
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	so that the head and breast are higher than the lower parts.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	so that the understanding is in this, that the injured part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to arrange what I say about great and minor wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, take what appears to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then have in your hands one pitiful minister who holds all the rupture in his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common way of suturing.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or needles, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave one or two fingers' width from the head of the wound and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two keys of the leather with the two keys of the scaphoid,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the leather inside, so that you make it pierce from that part.
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and bring together the two heads of the scaphoid into three parts;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain it with a doubled thread around the needle on both sides,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and bring together the two edges of the wound naturally,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave one or two fingers' width, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread just as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this as long as you need needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is bound.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and the needles be minor, between fine and coarse,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the fine needles pierce all the flesh, and those that are too coarse cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be minor;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it does not seem right to thrust the needles too far into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	lest they pierce and open the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the ends of the needles, so that they do not harm the patient in their sleep,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or drapes on the ends of the needles to keep them from moving.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them so that the wound is sewn;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this way of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because one or two needles suffice.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second suture is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you bring together the two edges of the leather and the two edges of the scaphoid together with a needle where there is a good strong thread,
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced all these edges into three parts,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then pull the needle through to the part where you began, in the manner that one sews cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a space of the thickness of a minor finger between each suture.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this suture is suitable for men,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed a wound that an ox had on its belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was wounded by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm of great size.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were well two palms of great size,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestine then, after it had been four hours later,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewn up just in fifteen days, and I healed it, and he became sound.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not heal him with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put clean cotton cloth on top of the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he became sound.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and thrust it from the outside part into the inside part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the correct spot straight on, then tie the head of the scaphoid or costal ligament where you have inserted the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side of the inside part straight to the outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as tailors do the pelts,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the scaphoid on one side and then pick it up again on the other, until the suture is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of suturing, which Galen says properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is when they assemble the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the heads of the scaphoid to the other head in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or proximate head of the mirror, and make it pierce that place alone.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two edges of the scaphoid;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside part to the inside part.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	of the two edges of the scaphoid;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from the outside part to the inside part, in two other edges of the mirror that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second way of suturing and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen says this phrase, and some bear witness to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one should sew the belly with two needles, or one where there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should thrust one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and knows that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is a suture more difficult than those of other places in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even as the fire has changed it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put back the intestine and the skin; then place on top the powder that fills the flesh,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the fire has changed it, then put on some ointment that is present, until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut off the thread, and be sewn the scaphoid and the mirror;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as with others, until he is sound.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, then put it on, as soon as it begins to spit brown water.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and stir it two times a day until he is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not make community with the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	so it is necessary that you moisten linen cloth lightly in temperate heat oil or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the wounds and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or purulence in his bowels, and many times this happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then catheterize him with black wine vinegar, and similarly if the purulence comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is more easily cured than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine which is called "jeune" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the putrefaction of the veins, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the approaching of its nature to that of dogs.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the gut jumps out of the wound, then put it back in place just like the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and turned green or black, then it is necessary that you tie the part that is black, so that no more blood may come forth.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the tie,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two ends hanging from the part below the wound until it is full and ready to ease the extraction when the guts fall out, and the wound bleeds.
de la routure dou boueil	of the flux of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is rough and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some people,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen that a man was wounded in the belly with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became ulcerated and turned into a fistula, and there came forth the excretion and the belching;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied a cure according to what I could, and did not cease from subtletizing until he was healed, and the bowels were sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it seal, I doubted that the patient had not evil in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better disposition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take fresh cloths from great tests, then gather up the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the cloth has opened the mouth, then put it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it stretches its mouth above;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then cut the string, and this holds so that he cannot undo it,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another cloth after in the same way as before, until the wound is entirely wrapped;
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	That head soars in the intestine, and does not bring any harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this thread of intestine which is quite worn out,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread one thread of fine linen twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then pass the thread through the needle, and sew up the intestine, and tighten it in the flux;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of sewing with cloths is no more than according to the path of trust and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the greater intestines, then there is no remedy nor health, except by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that all wound or abscess, when it ulcerates, is universally called "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and likewise when it has formed and flows with blood.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the verdant node's fault, hard and white, or where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it also flows like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it pours forth clear blood, and at other times thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and at other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and there is no scar,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is not except through one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its evil nature;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard scab inside and above the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much blood;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the bowels are corrupted, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the property in the region being slow to digest, and slow to heal, and flowing by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and signs, and remedies of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of fistula which is done by hand work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the bladder, or to the intestine, or to the kidneys, or to some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal member and similar parts.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of difficult healing, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come just to what I have said, and you have faith in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it with certainty, take a tent of earth or iron, if the fistula is straight, and clean it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then search for a fine tent of cloth,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the plover folds its movements around the tortuosity;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many perforations and you cannot well search it by touch.
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you cleanse it through one of the perforations,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because the moisture so short from one perforation to another and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you should bleed according to your power, knowing whether there is bone or nerve, and it is cut extremely deep.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and once you know truly the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein;
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I told you, cut according to what I told you.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the bad humors and corrupted juices that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then care for it until it is healed.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well opened in the right place, so it is necessary that you cut extremely deep, as far as you can.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put moist cloths on in medical poultice and tie them just to the top of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine dissolves the superfluity that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put unguents in gentle manner on healthy flesh, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves do not injure or main principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then remove the flesh until all corruption is removed.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then care for it with gentle remedies until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed and returns to being inflamed as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet finished enough.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	and uncover and cut until you reach the bottom.
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	if not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to proceed;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	and there's no other remedy except through natural decay.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone and you can extract it with pincers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then extract it with an instrument suitable for this.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, then remove them all, leaving none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture makes it contrary and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then cut the moist flesh and bone, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then apply the wound with gentle poultice.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will be easier to remove.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as the one in the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	then remove only the corruption until all blackness is removed.
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is great part of the corrupted bone and it comes just to the level of the marrow.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it is necessary to scrape and cut all the way to the corruption, and then care for it until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in one man's leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of around 30 years old who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the matter came to the leg and was swollen with a large abscess, and he had no reason to believe it would not open.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the doctors, driven by their foolishness, worked so much above that the abscess opened.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and in it corrupted a great deal of matter, and became a fistula, and many perforations came that all flowed with foul liquid from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many doctors applied treatment for about two years, and there was no improvement in the art of healing,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called in, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and all that flowed from the perforations had great power.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the flesh of the young man became red and had a citron-like color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I put a tent in one of these perforations, and then searched all the perforations.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that some were opening into others from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I then hastened, and cut in one of the perforations until I uncovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and it was corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came just to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I scraped away what appeared from the corrupted bone, and believed that there was no other corruption except for what I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines over a long time, but could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then resumed, and uncovered the bone as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and scraped it away, and then removed it, and ceased trying to heal the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and then removed it to its very marrow.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicines; and it was healed and closed quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it was no longer necessary to continue the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and out of fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For through the evacuation, he often bled, but he was healed entirely.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in the place of the bone, a hard flesh arose, and he was of good disposition and had no harm or contraindication whatsoever, neither to eat nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be scraped away in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a thread and strain it at the top of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to extend it upwards.
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and take another thread of linen, larger than the first thread, and tie it over the flesh that is above the bone.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the top, so that you can remove the corrupted flesh below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the skin where you see the hair growing, lest it wound the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a glowing iron or a heated plate below the bone to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to stay and see as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and then wait again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part;
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	so uncover all the flesh; then place a glowing iron below,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then stay on one side and the other until the corruption is purged away to its length in a pot, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupted joint and stay on the bone where it contains from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut it;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the fingernail of the hand or in the toenail, then that is very strong indeed;
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless it is necessary for you to question that corruption as to how it opens up;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but not so as to cause opposition from the vein or nerve.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the instruments and the fires for cutting these bones are many, according to the structure of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each kind of operation;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the manners of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument which you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can be dislocated due to internal or external causes;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have tried medicinal treatment for that corruption and it does not help,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cut off that member up to the point where the corruption comes;
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient may escape either by death or by evil, which is greater, namely the defect of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the sign is that the member becomes black, so it seems as though it has been burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after that blackness, then this corruption of member spreads to member;
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes over the whole body; so you must hasten to cut off.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if this is due to the sting of certain venomous beasts, such as the sea scorpion and viper and similar ones;
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corruption is at the head of the joint, then cut it off and do not give him space to reach as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches as far as the hand, then cut it off at the wrist, so that the corruption does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it reaches the arm, then cut it off at the shoulder; and if it passes beyond the shoulder, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy except for the quantity of his virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and so too with the foot: if the corruption comes to the first joint, then cut it off after the second joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it reaches the foot, then cut off the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it climbs up to the thigh, then cut off at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy except to let the patient die quickly.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of cutting or staying the member is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch one minister down from one tie, and another minister up from the other tie,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you uncover the flesh that is between the two ties with a wide spatula, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or stay it, and place a linen cloth on either side, so that the blood does not touch the healthy skin.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another wound and abscess comes to the patient soon.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs when you work, then cauterize the area hastily,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or put some restraining powders on top; then return to your treatment until it is complete.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man in his own foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he got a blackness that seemed like burning fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption came first to his ankle bone of the foot, until it reached all the way up to the foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cut off his foot and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that, the corruption came again to the joint of his hand, and he came to me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things that would cause repercussions after purifying the body, but the corruption could not cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not wish to, because I had hope of reperfusing the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the man's virtues were weak; and he became despairing of all, and returned to his own land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and then he hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have this tale only because it is done for another's need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes to a hard flesh and remains so long that it makes a great gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then bursts and opens, and the pus jumps out, and leaves the flesh as white as a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is also smooth as a delicate piece of cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and do not reach as far as the bone, nor as far as the nerve, and such diseases are called "sain".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called a "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it reaches as far as the bone in front, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is like this: you cut that skin all around, and similarly when it is smooth as a piece of cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not hurt because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin will hurt, and the corruption is not in front,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And the skin is covered with flesh, so treat a pustule thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look to see if the breasts are large and the nipple that is in it has a foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then apply Egyptian medicine which is made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take aloes, and oil, and litharge, in equal parts, and put to cook in one vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take what you need from this, and mix it with water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use it to fumigate the breast, and restrain the ulcer;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine sit for two hours, then strain it out by expressing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breasts are purified and the foul odor is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and never once use ashes' water for fumigating;
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes from the vine's wood, and pour water upon them;
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it flow, and use it to fumigate, until you know that the breasts are well purified;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear this, nor the Egyptian medicine nor water of ashes;
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	so make a fumigation with water and honey, or add a small amount of litharge to it;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you fumigate with honey and sweet wine, which the honeys have the property of purifying and cleansing;
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wines make the skin clear;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breasts are well purified;
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	so fumigate with what brings forth flesh in it;
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and take defined plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you fumigate with some medicines and unguents, the properties of which I have said or to treat unguents;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the ulcer on the breast is small, and the plug from the fumigator cannot enter into it;
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	so enlarge it with a small iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or balsamic ointment, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, so cut and leave just one small opening or enough for the fumigator to enter;
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the ulcer that discharges milk is above, then cut or make it lower than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the milk is in full flow, do not let flesh form;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut beneath the breast as you see;
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	so prepare it in such a way that the milk flows down to the lowest part where it is;
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the milk is in full flow, do not let flesh form;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut beneath the breast as you see;
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so prepare it in such a way that the milk flows gently down and does not leave any of the milk behind;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and apply it on a linen cloth that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut at the strongest spot of the ulcer on the breast, making it one small notch larger than the first;
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply a soothing ointment on another cloth according to the size of the ulcer,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on the breast ulcer to ease the milk flow, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days, once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that which is on the breast ulcer, is often removed in order to stop the milk flow,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and knows what comes from the milk, whether it be venom or a little or enough or digested or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take care to see if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not;
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been thus applied and you see the nature that appears on the breast ulcer,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	so know that the breasts are already healed, and are approaching health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loosen it in the morning or on the third day, and when you remove the dressing;
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	so change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts discharge undigested milk after many days, know that the breasts are not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons appear late after a long time, do not despair of health;
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health is approaching. For there are men whose flesh takes time to form in their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested milk jumps from the breast after many days, know that the breasts are not healed;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts take time to clear up and are inflamed, then apply medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue;
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as defined ointment, for it has a great part of vinegar, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take defined ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and rose of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and this same thing makes honey cooked to increase.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when defined ointments are not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then glue it to a cloth, and put it on the breast, and never once administer it with aristology for a long time;
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lily of heaven, which is also like wheat flour and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use it with simple or compound medicines: grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is long-lasting and is not healed by this treatment;
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption has gone deep, and makes an impression on the bone, or causes stiff limbs, or breaks tendons;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	so apply the treatment for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the apostema of the lung
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Fulness is an apostema that arises under the lung of the finger pulp of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or perhaps it arises in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and not taken care of, then a foul apostema comes;
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and runs and discharges milk until it reaches the root of the lung, and perhaps even all the way through.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion all the way to the bone, until there is a stinking pain, and the head of the shoulder is wide apart, and the color is faint.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help.
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	so you must remove all the superfluity that remains of the swelling.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is very great help if the bone is sound, and the swelling is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the swelling pushes into the flesh, and begins to prick, and bleed.
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	so you must put the rule under the swelling that pricks the flesh.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and tie it up tight, and cut away that subtle and lightly-skinned flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining skin medicines burning and corrosive in order to remove all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it away and treat further, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the shoulder bone corrupting, then cut it away in one piece just as was said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is festering and bound, and it feels great pain, then you must heal it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the swelling of the spatula-like part by cutting across above.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and beware that the cut does not come all the way to the skin that is under the swelling, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The shoulder joint that arises in the hands of some men by chance is all fatty.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is a place where it has bones, and sometimes it has swelling.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them are born at the root of the joint, or in certain parts of the shoulders.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born in any part of the shoulder does not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and he who is born at the joint of the shoulder, by chance moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the movement of one who is fatty is light, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula-like instrument.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is hard to cure: it's best not to cut it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or has a swelling at the back of the shoulder, you must first cut away the skin all the way to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with a suitable thread for this purpose, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes to the shoulders together comes by birth, or by sudden injury, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cut away that swelling, and then the shoulder will repair itself according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or moist cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not swell.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of cloth, until the wound is closed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to any of his shoulders with the palm, then cut away that swelling as it should be.
Des vils	Of evils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Wounds are great and swollen lumps full of melancholy excess that come to many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk on foot and who work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to them sometimes purging with oil of cole, and then heal them with the balm of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron treatment is according to two manners: one is when you cut and then drain the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you open the vein and let it bleed all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cut is according to this manner: first arise the leg of hot water very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned out.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then strain the leg of the patient from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then lift and let out all the black blood at your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient's virtue can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it off, and command him to keep eating flesh and drinking black oil.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and start the evacuation and healing again when the veins are full and it hurts the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The alleviation of pain is according to this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and raise the leg of hot water until it becomes red, and swell the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have a bath, heat it over the fire, and then cut into the vein of the long part at the top of the kneecap, or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then apply oil to the skin, and scrape the vein from each part, until it appears when you touch it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then tie the thread underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then anoint it lightly with oil.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut into another place above the three shoulders; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it up with the thread, just as you did, and anoint it with another oil, just as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another incision, or more if you need it, then lift it up and cut into the shoulder of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then drain it and lift it up to the second incision; then draw it out from incision to incision, until it comes out all at once, then cut.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you can't drain and lift it, put an awl through each strong double thread.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie and drain it, and put underneath one thread, and turn your hand to the left and right, until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it doesn't cut, for if it cuts, one can no longer drain or lift it, and it will cause harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drained it all, put on the place of the wound a moist cloth soaked in wine and rose oil; and care for him until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and looped together all at once, and it's not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	so it is necessary that you cut it obliquely, but do not cover it up; and treat it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut through, so that it opens up the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of great curvature, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
De la voinne civile	Of civil blood
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is placed in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and on earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it occurs in another part than in the legs, and this happens due to the purulence that comes from under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as if it came inside the body like snakes and worms, inserted between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the skin changes color and the vein begins to come out, like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the lump appears, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of linen cloth, from one inch to two and a half inches, and tie it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it seems to be coming out from behind, wrap it around the cloth and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root until it is all out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause abscess and purulence at the same place, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it is necessary that she be treated little by little until the very end, and no part of her remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and it is sometimes this vein when it is treated with five or ten paces long,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, from whom it issued 10 paces long, and when you cut it, it bursts into 1 vein or pore, and penetrates right down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all comes out; and let the matter inside be emptied, and apply to the place medicines that prevent purulence for some time, then cure it as you would abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein goes to the joints of the foot, or into the foot itself,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes out in many pores, and from which it jumps out; then cure it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of the worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This illness is called in our land "disease of the ox", because it often affects oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes up and down through the whole body.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and one feels it well as it moves from member to member, until it breaks through the skin where it goes and jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by purulence of certain humors, such as come from worms and serpents and lice and ascarids or the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts of its malice, for when it goes through the body and climbs to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance it returns, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and treated, one cannot be sure except when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong cord tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above and treat the wound, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you cannot find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire above, until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near to the eye, then hold a mirror under it sharply, and cut above, and treat the wound.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient in purgation of the body with soluble medicines to purge the bad humors poured out.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of meats that cause purulence.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and about an hour later, I saw it rise like a worm on the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than anything else, just as bright silver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it ran throughout the body, until it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was winding around the body again, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very much astonished at how she was moving from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this illness behave in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen many cases where the pain would move from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it like that in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought to myself that it was because the woman's body was dry and her veins were uncovered.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore that windiness appeared constrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not appear according to this reason in those who are delighted and have moist bodies and veins that respond.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see the disease cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then tie above and below quickly, and then cut above until that constrained windiness comes out.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you don't see it at your hands,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then cure it with those things that resist windiness, such as stinking pills and pills of serapin, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of Arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are those which have great points, and small, and hairy, and soldered;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those who have two corners, and of those who have tongues, and of those which have fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which falls in any member if it falls according to two manners: or in principal member, falls
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, womb, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you next, warn:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so it is necessary that you be warned against the extraction of this arrow, for many die afterwards in various conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not warn you at all, and the arrow is not in the deepest part, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and jumps out the sinciput which is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is blindness and deafness and swelling and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of gall;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is without force in the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it affects speech and voice;
