et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps from the moist white wound resembling polyps, and also jumps as if burned charcoal;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign warns you, then hold back from the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it's not too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the shaft when it hits the heart is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not at all empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the shaft moves as if polyps, and in black blood, and comes with coldness and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	know then without doubt that death is present.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that does not pierce the womb is when foam-free it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits the covering of the chest, it is on the little ribs; and pours out great gall and great pain and breathes heavily; and all the members of the shoulders are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something from undigested food jumps out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the belly, and there is no hope of passing anything through the intestines, then there is no hope for the cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow hits the bladder, and urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the face and shoulders and throat and arms and shoulder and aid and spine of the back and fore-arm and calf and knee and legs, and similar members are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you, because that happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man whose arrow hit him on the eyelid in the root of the eye:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and pulled it out on the other side under the fatty earlobe, and he was healed without numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out an arrow that hit him in the fatty eyelid under the paper-thin skin below,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was bent, and I could not pull it out except for the tip towards the wood,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was as big as a Turkish bowstring, all of very light iron without ears; the joint was healed, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was the Arab arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I filed down the barbs, and made it subtle until I pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out an arrow from one man whose it had struck in the belly, and thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after it had passed thirty days, his condition did not change at all;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and extracted it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see one man whose an arrow has hit him on the back, and the wound is bound up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside, and does not change his natural disposition,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you see one other man whose an arrow has hit him on the face, and the wound is bound up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I pulled out an arrow from one of the king's princes, whose it had struck in the eye;
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly bent to the right side; and the arrow was entirely bent.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned for treatment three days after it was struck. I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for it with all a subtle tentacle, and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought that it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the place an ointment attracting and digestive, because the flesh did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the arrow's tip.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the ointment for many days, and the wound healed above, and the patient remained thus for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so that he felt the arrow one day inside his eye; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a medicine with corrosive properties for many days, until it was open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tested it, and felt the head of the arrow which was bent at the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pushed it into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it passed beyond the boundaries for three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then it fell out of the wound and I stuck in tongs, pulling it from one side and the other, and it could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not stop subtlety and extracting with tools, until I got it one day with well-made tongs,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, so I will follow it, and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your cure on what I do not say, for books cannot learn everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters know well a little thing, and about what is present and failing,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	and true nine works, and nine instruments, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not emerge from members where they are fixed unless according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the way in which they enter, or by some other side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out to one side where it enters is an arrow entering the fleshy parts, and sometimes it jumps out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, then let it stay until the flesh is surrounded, and the exit is eased;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is fixed in the bone and cannot come out, then let it stay thus for some days, and move each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps out, and if it does not jump, then pierce all around one subtle furrow, until the flesh around is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes just to one of the vents of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: then do not pull it out at all, but let it stay equal after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes just to the skull, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is fixed only in the bone and does not come just to the skull,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient stays some days without bad accident, then extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very fixed and cannot come out at all, then apply poultices around, as I have said; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is embedded in the flesh of the body and one cannot see it, then search for it everywhere.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you find it, then extract it with some suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then make it wider until the wound is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and extract the arrow if you can, and if there are ears in the arrow where it stays.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	so cut away the flesh that is fixed from both sides to as much as you can;
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can extract it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and do it subtly so that you don't break the arrow, which would be pulled out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until the flesh around is softened, and then extract it, for the extraction will be eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the haemorrhaging of blood makes you contraindicated, then apply what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting into the nerve and vein, and devise how you can extract the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or soon or late, or firmly or gently; and put the patient in the shape he was in when the arrow hit him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest aid that can be; and if you cannot, then put him in accord with what the signs show to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another side, or shows some sign of it, or the skin is swollen in front so that one can see or feel it in an unusual way:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then above, until the forceps can take hold, and then pull it out: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it for a while, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the head of the arrow is stuck, then push it through to the entire head;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the head breaks off and you need to administer binding, then apply one instrument that is toothed,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the bristle of the instrument; and then push it through.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is broken, then apply one instrument with an entering point, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as seems fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow breaks or stays or is lodged in the belly or bladder or ribcage, and it is close, and you can cut above, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and take care not to cut the vein or nerve, and then pull it out, and then dress the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium-sized, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the toothed instrument is also like the feather of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push against the point of the arrow, as shown here in this form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps for pushing and for cutting is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins through which one is cleansed, thirty-one, of which there are sixteen at the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to know: two batons that are behind the ears, which are called "herbeches";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two eyelids of the two eyes, which are called "aspirations";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins that are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lip above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherics";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins commonly used for bleeding are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, and it is located on the left side, and the common people call it "the vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the median one is called "Fasce", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and the common people call it "the vein of the heart"; and the basilic one is located on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it "the vein of the belly", and it is above the scapula.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that one used for bleeding, which appears openly above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the auricular and annular veins, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is located below the fold of the right armpit,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous one that is at the ankle of the right side, and the vein called "nesse" which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are after the ears helps ancient catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the bleeder, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a screw,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two little folds depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	which then bend towards your back and where you feel the pulse under your back, it begins to swell;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and pierce below the vein just up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein above.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and peel the skin and the vein well two fingers' breadth across, and make it come out of blood until you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and bind it, until it is clean;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth for ancient migraines,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and headaches, and accustomed ophthalmia, and at the root of old tears to those.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the bleeder is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient tightens his neck, until the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse under your back, and then it begins to swell;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the skin above the vein at the level of your backbone's index, and pierce the lancet below.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein up, and cut it, just as you have done with two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your hand on the vein for an hour, then put a cotton cloth on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it tightly, and let it be until it is clean; and we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the forehead vein is worth just as much as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for ancient facial diseases, and for migraines, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fossae", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck and bind the vein until it is clean, and never once allow a wide inflammation.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not good for the inflammation to be too severe; and the vein should not be torn in two, because the bone is close, and by chance, the inflammation may break through when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the two eyelids helps those with eyes, and with ringworm, and with redness, and with ulcers in the eye, and with facial diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting with some kind of ligature, just as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then bleed, and let the bleeding be about the width of a finger, a little longer than the inflammation is wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the inflammation is subtle, it may break through; then let the blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind with cotton, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding of the navel vein is worth for ague, and for feigned headache, and for facial diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	just as migraines and redness that come to the face, and similarly when it is ancient.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck, then presses his navel with your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a subtle flame long, and stick it between the two nostrils, in the space that is between them.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will start flowing now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and don't go too deep into it, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for a night, because it is very quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bleeding of the two inguinal veins helps with the constriction of the uterus, and with the beginning of menstruation, and with many diseases, and with epilepsy, and with corroding, and with herpes.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck below one and the other, just as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing above the patient's head, and the patient sit on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then bleed the vein of the length a little widely, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as is needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the same on the other vein, then release the ligature, and bind the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not choke; and let it be until morning, when the wound is clean.
De la sainie des leivres	On the bleeding of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins above the lips so helps to clot in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and nose bleedings and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is to have the patient sit before you, and hold their neck as I said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right side of the lip and the other on the left side.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small dark veins.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then grasp one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then grasp the largest one on each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding of the veins that are under the tongue so helps after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it's at the constriction of the throat, and with diseases of the uvula, and with diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts their tongue, and looks down on each side at a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then bleed one and the other, and do not go too far in depth, because below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the throat which are commonly bled are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pricking with one small and broad flame of myrtle or olive, as they cut through the throat, and is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are large and subtle according to the largeness and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the myrtle flame is very well known, and it is large as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And has need to open the veins that are smooth and full of thick blood visible, and which contain thick and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pricked, and is for bleeding the subtle veins where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the cephalic vein, which is one of these veins, so helps with diseases that are under the throat, and at the neck, and at the chest, and at the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the bleeder that he should bleed slightly, and beware of the artery which is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and blood comes forth in abundance, then it is necessary to stop it, as I said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and one must not prick the flame, but cut as with anesil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the cephalic vein does not open clearly, then it is necessary that you should pull it out, and change another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want any part of it, or you bleed in place of it the vein in the arm: it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut with the flame of anesil, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see the place where the bleeding is occurring, then it is necessary that you should pull out the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with a sign, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the flame of anesil;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not cut into the artery when you see the place swelled, for it is an artery; then withdraw.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it come forth above like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and put your finger on top for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, as often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	then bind the arm and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be careful, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it flows, and it gushes out, and medicine is not present to you, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head of it retreats; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a strip of fig tree bark, and split it, and take one half and bind well until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the blood is stopped, that's good; if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of the bleeding is not difficult in many dispositions for the small wound of the cut and the power of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The bleeding of the vein in the middle so helps that it treats blood from above, and from below the head.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the bleeder to beware of the nerve which is below, and if he pricks too deeply, and finds the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the bleeding may be stopped, but by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, then it is necessary that you should bleed from the instrument of anesil; and withdraw the nerve as far as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it longwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bleeding of the cephalic vein so helps that it treats blood from the head, and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed by pricking with the olive flame or the myrtle flame, because it is the most safe of all the veins, for there are no nerves or arteries below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek out the lightest place and not harm anything if it does not work the first time, and one begins again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance the places swell up in some people, when one tries it for the first time, but it does not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing that you should know about bleeding, is that it is not necessary only for the purpose of preserving health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent diseases from coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins that are in the throat: namely, the cephalic, facial, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed at the beginning of prayer time in the morning, and after eating in autumn and winter when the signs of repletion appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should bleed either on the first or third day after 2 or 3 hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The wound that is administered to the sick person has no fixed time determined, but rather whenever need arises by day or by night, in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to heal children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman carrying more than three-quarters of the way through her seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And one should not heal the old who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be healed, in whatever way it may be, it is necessary that he cleanse the intestines with a light enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has many bad humors retained, so that the veins do not draw off the superfluities from the intestines, which are harmful to the main members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor does one heal who is too full of meat, nor drunk, as long as they are in such a state, nor dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and one does not heal after passion of the belly, and vomiting, and purging of the stomach, and frequent habit with a woman, and travail, watching, and menstruating, and all that comes from bodily virtue, or by something of the arm or body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtlety the humors, if the blood is thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter a bath, unless something hinders it, to subtlety the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal from the vein of the belly around the third hour, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day free from labor, and toil, and luxury, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be laid and joyful, and let the doctor's hands be higher than those whom one is healing, and wipe the arm twice or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then stretch the ligament above moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then wipe the place with hands until the veins swell and one feels them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the doctor's finger with a little old oil, then put his right hand on that vein below the place where one wants to heal.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not fade and fail when cutting.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flow like strings to be cut, and those that are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the finger on it, it withdraws the finger, and cannot open the vein, and thus one is of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, it is too narrow a wound, therefore it is necessary that the doctor be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens at first time, it is good; if not, then one must begin again a little below or above that place in haste, unless the swelling of the limb.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the patient is frightened, then one should leave it for a day or two and not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	in case there may come abscesses soon; nor enter into a bath, then begin again the healing if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtlety and you doubt that it will not be as much blood as you see, then trust in that very opening with all the right flow.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work a little hastily, until the limb is swollen; for it often happens that way, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swollen, then do not begin again to heal, and put a little layer of oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and is more nourishing in this place than the cloth that the oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the cloth of oil in each healing that you heal the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing is done with treacle and balm of earth, when one puts it on the limb; and subtlety the blood and divides when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when it is not healed except at that time or the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	so hasten, and put a wet sponge on the limb in water and seed broth, and strain it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it remains at the limb for some days with no blackness or greenish color, then it will not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on some thing of aloe or myrrh mixed with the juice of camphor, mastice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often it happens that an abscess and appearance arise in the healing of the wound: put then your hand on it, and if you find the limb soft to the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So take care that you do not put on anything of what we have said, for by chance the blood flow of the artery is cut; but apply one dry poultice to harden the limb, then cure it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to its quantity and virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it become subtlety; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for that person who is fat and strong, and has need of bloodletting, to have a larger wound, and the fingers be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for that person who is weak, do the opposite, and let it be healed little by little, and have it healed by cutting across, not by piercing;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of healing is safe from purging of blood and cutting of nerve, and is more worthy than the healing of the long or the wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to that person whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give moist bread in the juice of green apples; if he is overheated, then treat the blood three times or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexion, then anoint before the healing with moist bread in a mazer syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-odored syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he pukes after the issue of much blood, then it is necessary that he drinks broth of charcoal and a subtle aromatic syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things that we have said in the chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to swell his arm and heal it another time, so it is fitting when it is weakened by great injury, that he heals it little by little, according to the quantity of his continued vigor.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to swell his arm after the first healing, and he has strong flesh, then he heals in .vij. hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wants to heal on another side, then he should heal in the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood inside the body that is already overheated, and makes one feverish; so it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and enlarge the opening as far as the pomegranate.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Then you should apply all the conditions of healing, and put your hand on his pulse as he heals, so that death does not come in place of pomegranate.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this often happens when the healer is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not happen when you want to loosen the arm and bring out blood the second time, and the opening is closed, unless you press strongly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	unless he is bent, then let him stretch out his arm quickly, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let him leave it alone until he heals the second time; or you should insert at the tip of the flame, until the blood that is frozen at the opening of the vein issues forth.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on one part of seal that has been put in water, and press upon it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then let it be and do not constrict it at all, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood the second time, then let him heal in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein within the arm is healed in the place of the head vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the scab becomes red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then let him heal now across, not at all across or long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and let him heal well close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then put his hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, then do not put his hand in hot water again, for one puts him more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the saved part of the right hand is worth more than all liver diseases, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, so that one may see;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the healing is across, and you close it completely all around, then it will not cause any harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep in front, for the nerves are beneath all of them denuded of flesh.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn blood as much as is needed, then put on the vein oil and seal to solder quickly, and so do for each part.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healing of the left hand is worth as much to the disease of mice, and do it just the same way as I told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The healing of the soporific is worth to all diseases that are beneath the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the kidneys, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and thighs, and legs old, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his healing is that the patient puts their foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it breaks down.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and lift above the ankle of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot there go out many veins.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	heal then the largest or the one at the ankle that is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are below, and the healing should be across as when sewing; and let the flames be anointed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the healer fails the first time, then try again the second at a little distance above, because the wound is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	nor doubt the nerves, as we have said, and so do the same with the soporific of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The wound of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its healing is worth to the pain of the groin when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its healing is that the patient enters or takes a bath, and stretches above the ankle four fingers while twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then let it heal in all ways that you can, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and is worth more than when you close it, for the wound is clean, and it has healed in many hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't believe me, then heal any vein that opens or is on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and let blood flow as much as you see fit, and then loosen the bandage, and put on cotton and stretch it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	(The text continues with a new section: "Of the Healings of Ventouses")
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or of iron, or of glass; and ventosation is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventosation which is without piercing is done in two ways: either it is all fire, or not on fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and ventosation which is done by piercing and extraction of blood is done in 14 places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is all on the top of the head; and the others are in the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on each side of the neck; and the ventouse below the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the ventouse on both shoulders; and the ventouse above the elbows.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the ventouses in both arms; and the ventouses of both legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the poultices of the two shins; and the lancing does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore one has not weakened it at all, as one would with a vein cure;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be administered, nor at all fire or sense of fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to lance, or for habituation, then we will administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and every time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to be lanced, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who swell up with repletion and redness on their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are some who swell up with a drop of blood in their mouth, and have puffed out the tongue, and spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who imagine, and see through bloody water, and are wounded, and mortally ill, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the midst of the month, we will then command to lance after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The purging of the mouth also helps with the swelling of the head... that comes from above, and it is not necessary for this to be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this lancing is in place of the purging of the head.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not necessary for someone who has a cold complexion to use this, or if they have cholera, because this does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not necessary for old people to use this, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from this often become oblivious, and therefore it is necessary to place the poultice a little lower down due to the doubt of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The lancing in the neck is in place of the purging of the head and the basilica, and therefore it is worth it for the constriction of the belly,
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to the tearing of the channel of the womb, and all over, and to repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to apply a little pressure, because if she holds too tightly, she may cause oblivion or constriction of the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The lancing at the two ribs of the neck is worth for the pains of the head, and eye pain and migraine, and to strangulation, and to pain in the roots of the teeth,
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in place of the purging of the basilica; and it is necessary that you command the servant to stretch out his hand when placing it, so he does not compress the artery, and does not come forth with bloody discharge.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The lancing below the chin is worth for mouth disease and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the purgings of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The lancing at the shoulders is worth for the disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The lancing of the sides is as good as three veins of the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it treats blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the servant not to pierce too deeply by front, because the skin is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The poultice that is on the buttocks is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases underneath, and it is necessary that the poultice be large and made of earth, so it can well draw out; and by chance, if they were subtle, they would break; and this would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The poultices of the legs clearly cure, because they draw out blood from all the body, and are worth for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and uterus, and restore the flowers; and they take the place of the two shins and two ankles, and although they weaken the body after long use, they cause dizziness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the poultice is that you first apply it empty, and then suck it temperately, and put it on hastily, and move it equally, and do not cease from doing so, until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the redness of the blood; then pierce, and remove the poultices, and take heed in the disposition of the body, because there are some who have tough skin, and clear pores: thus it is necessary to strike once only, and make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to pierce a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, we only suffice once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we often recommence; and if the blood is thick, we pierce in deep, and the end is that the heart should be pierced suddenly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for one who has thick skin and hard, and who have large pores, that you anoint the edges of the poultices with oil that is aperitive and dissolutive:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, with oil of violets, or with oil of sweet almonds, or with oil of cucumber seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, with oil of parsley, or of lily, or of chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter oil, or balmy oil, or oil of aniseed, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person to be cured has tender skin and large pores, there is no need to apply oil,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And the person who has a lot of moisture, should rise easily with water of myrtle, or water of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should rise with old wine, or water of sycamore, or a decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or other similar ones;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to apply a poultice before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the application.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary for him to guard himself when he needs to be purged and when he is being purged.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of that person who has a choleric temperament, and whose blood is too thick and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it is necessary for him to take cold things, such as grapes, endive, and lettuce, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink a little, and pork of the shoulder, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And that person who has a cold complexion, so take honey syrup and aromatic wine of medium age, which is between old and new, and drink a little, and drink a little, and small birds and wrens.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day when he will be purged, so he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people treacle or muscatel at times before purging, or after, to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be thinned out, but it does not need to be drunk by those who are hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The poultices that are applied without striking a blow are those that are applied on the liver, and on the kidneys, and podagra, and on the belly and the navel and the reins and the haunches, for those members do not bear to be struck there.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one only does this in order to attract blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	just as we put them on the breasts when the milk flows; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put poultices on the belly and on the navel to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it takes away the pain when there is inflammation or piercing, and by its attracting power it takes away the inflammation, or brings the piercing back to its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and on the kidneys when there is retained flatulence,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these poultices are administered empty in order to suck only once; and sometimes they are administered with hot fire, and sometimes with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	just as in diseases of the tear duct, and in such a way that one fills the poultice with hot water or cold water in which herbs suitable for this purpose have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the poultice administered to fire is this:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two fingers of width and half a palm in depth, and it has on the border around the middle a small notch, just as for pushing an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it is of clay, soft before so that it does not hurt the patient when applied to the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and it has in the middle a bar of clay or iron, to put a candle enclosed,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they are great and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the poultices of children are different from those of old people, and of thin ones from those of fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must thus apply this poultice to the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candle of wax or one linen thread, and put it inside the poultice across the bar that is inside the poultice,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light may be at the bottom of the poultice so that it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and the two fingers should be on the notch that we have said, so that when one wants to, the vapor goes out, and one removes the poultice.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and one takes the linen thread just as before, and renews it often, if you need it.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the poultice then which is administered in disease of tear duct, it has no bar nor notch, and is only applied when it is filled with water, and is put on the member alone.
et c’est li forme:	and that's the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sutures are only applied when one cannot put poultices because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare bones, such as knuckles or nipples, and other similar ones;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find sutures that are in clean water without stirring, then take them.
