et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a vessel with sweet water, until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cleansed with vinegar and poultice, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the sutures.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and tight, if it is a place where one can put a poultice, then put one there, for this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then take the limb with ease, and then with water, very well, and then stretch it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb swells too much after the sutures, then soak one cloth of linen in cold water, and put it on, until the swelling subsides.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the swelling is multiple, then put on vitriol crushed or gall, and similar things, until it subsides.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the limb a half of peeled broad beans, and leave them until they dry out at the limb, which will now subside.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other sutures.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the sutures will not take hold, then rub the limb with fresh blood, or drive a needle in until the swelling goes away.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and soon as they feel the blood, they will dry out.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are falling off, then powder on a little bit of alum and burnt silk, or ash, so that they will stick now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a treatment for fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen, dear son, that foolish men who do not read this chapter will never see any of the ancient books nor letters about it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is strange the science in our land, for I never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it, except through the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the subject, and through experiment, and through the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and abbreviated it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of instruments that are applied, just as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore fitting that we say the prologue of this book, summarizing the words and chapters where wise men put their understanding, and rest upon virtue, so that those who are proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a breakage or dislocation or twisting or cracking comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to hasten to heal the patient from one side and the other, if nothing else can be done, such as weakness of the body, or children, or old men;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the weather is not very cold, or too hot; and thin cholers, that is to say, cold fluxes, and flesh of hare and of kid, and does not drink wine, nor thin fat meats, and does not fill oneself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about a warm abscess, or spreading of matter to the member; so revives the patient in his former government which he used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary for you to nourish the patient with meats that make a great healing, or if he has viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and testicles, and pies, and pork belly, and eel, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this nourishment brings strength and makes the breakage heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of old men and decrepit people cannot be well reunited or soldered according to their nature due to the weakness of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as children's bones.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but don't worry, reset the broken bone with a thick splint that sets and joins the member together, until it is strong as it was before; and don't neglect his work, and therefore he should be nourished with big meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breakages are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the breakage of the head is one thing, and the breakage of the ribs or leg is another, and I will tell you in this chapter all the kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breakages that occur by rotation, and others by flexion, such as the cutting of a feather to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with wound, and breakage in a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own method, and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory recalls in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the breakage of the bone is by twisting, and appears well by feeling, and sounds under the pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting nor sounding at the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no breakage;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or cracking, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So it is not necessary for you to move him with your hand, but set aside the remedies that come later and then restrain him subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breakage that occurs by rotation, and are the two parts disjointed, it is necessary to put them back together now, so that warm abscesses may come;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if warm abscesses come, then let him rest a day or two until the abscess is appeased;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then set him back together so that he can move lightly and wisely, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restorations of those who have fragments; then restrain him, as is necessary later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone has broken pieces, and two parts are separated, whether it be in arm or leg, or that it is one of small members, or two strings, or one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member in its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the member are dislocated, then reset by all means the additions in their place with your hand, and take care that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join well the two joints of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel with your hand if it seems to you that he is not well: so adjust him nicely, and do not strain him too much, nor press as those who bring forth by their work warm abscess and contraction to the member, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in place, so chastise the patient well that he does not move it, neither while awake nor while sleeping, nor while turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the member is so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and it must be set in such a condition that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is set correctly, so that twisting does not come when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken member are according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: so it is necessary to envelop them in soft and subtle linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are big, such as thighs and legs: so it is necessary to envelop them in a wide and strong linen, for the wide linens encompass all the great member and restrain it from all parts equally, so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie around with light cloths, three or four turns according to the member, and restrain your hand slightly on all the linen, then go up above the breakage and restrain less, so that the breakage will move away a bit.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the linen a little and a little, until you take up a great part of the healthy flesh, then take another linen and turn it around again on top of the broken bone;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the breakage, and restrain moderately, neither too strongly nor too gently, as we have said in the first lesson above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the linens and cloths, so that it is all even, then tie everything together with one bandage, and then put your well-made bandages on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, then put on something soothing for the warm abscess, and which removes the swelling, and let it be like that for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then restrain on your bandages, and be of the thickness of half a well-filled cane, or of gut which is used to make buttons, or of palm leaf fibers, and be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the bandage which one puts on the breakage be a little bigger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it is necessary for the member, whether small or great.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it above the stars just as you did at the first touch, then lay it above a thread in harmony, just as you did at the first touch above the bridle.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is in this case, the looser; and it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, like I have seen in the works of fools who make their own strings from twisted linen cord, and it's a great error, because the string cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it's not necessary that there should be less than two fingers' width between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is hurt by the edges of the stars after the stretching in their own flesh, then he puts under them poultices made of linen or ragged wool, so that he does not injure himself.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bridle, and the bowstring is broken, I will say how to treat it hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it's not necessary to stretch all the members on the first day of a broken bone.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, it's not necessary to put stars on them except after five or six days, or more according to the safety of abscesses that often happen.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and behold the manner of ancient poultices to restore breaks, dislocations, and torsions: it is that you take flour that remains at the walls of the mill, and mix it with an abundance of eggs, and put this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and it's the common manner of the poultice restoring breaks in many dispositions, and especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of poultice restoring breaks and dislocations and torsions: take aloes, ladanium, and myrrh, and asafoetida, and gum arabic, and mugwort, each 20 times; and mirre and aloe, each 5 times; and alechil 9 times; and make powder, and mix it with an abundance of eggs; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this poultice, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is valuable to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of poultice that is valuable for torsion: take mugwort and visnag, each 20 times; mirre and aloe, each 8 times; asafoetida 6 times; Armenian balm 10 times, and pound well, and mix with water or an abundance of eggs, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of poultice for joints and bones that have come out of their places, and calms the pain that follows, and helps to use the bone, and bridle: take new wool, and soak it in ale and cooked oil, and put it on the joint. This poultice does not restore, but it is good for calming a hot abscess, and properly removes pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of poultice that restores broken bones: take dried leaves of fig and leaves of terrestrial sycamore, and pound them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of poultice for the restoration of bone breaks and to reduce the remaining abscess. Take root of visnag, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of vine, each one part; and pound, and mix with wine, and if the member is heated, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another manner of poultice even stronger than the first, when abscesses that are hard to break come to restore the member. Take roots of visnag, and flaxseed, balm, melilot, and sansuc, and flowers of violets and camomile, each one part; and pound, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on the broken member to restore it except with a wax and oil ointment, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two extremes, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken member to restore it, things that are slightly warm and dry, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of poultice that is valuable for wound and pain: take mugwort and human hair or bird quill, and visnag, and equal amounts, and pound them together, and make a poultice and the bandage.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen the bandage a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if so, do not loosen the bandage for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, you hasten and loosen the bandage, and remove the poultice now; and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and plunge it into water, and lift up the place until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind with a cloth, until you are sure of a hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member subside, and be removed the pain, then resume the subtle binding and a little poultice, and do not strain it too hard as before; and bind subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess and redness and pain and swelling have disappeared from all of it, and you need poultice and binding again, then start again, just as you did first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the member, then do not loosen it more than after three days or four days or five days or six days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what is seen, until the breakage sets in and approaches the union with flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then hold the member more tightly than before, and let its flesh grow fat, as I said before; and if you see the place drying out more than is necessary, know that there will be no nourishment for it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then wash the place with hot water daily, every time you loosen it, and gently ease out a little of the binding.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	By this work, then, the nourishment is cut off from the member, and hasten to do what fools' physicians do, which leaves the member twisted: that's bad, and it's painful work, and I see nothing else but tiring and working improperly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of diverse methods of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many methods of breakings are, and diverse forms, and the causes are assigned;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for there are breakings that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the arm breaks off all the bone just up to the joint that is under the bone, as happens with an axe or a fist; and therefore this manner of breaking is called "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone above, without piercing, and is called this manner of breaking "absolute"; and the wounds from these two breakings are great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or splitting or breaking of the arm or leg bone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persevering break, which approaches just to the skin that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is opened in the bone as thin as a hair, and it is a small splitting, and therefore this breaking is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by striking with a stone or by falling or by similar thing, and causes the bone piece to enter downward, and it is like when blacksmiths heat metal on their forges; so the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often with those who have soft bones, such as the head of an infant;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and this happens in all these manners of breaking where small pieces are broken off so that they are like that; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manners of breakings by the stripping above them, and the probing that is attempted, and by the flesh that is corrupted which is on.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by this: when the bone is uncovered and one rubs it gently above, then the black break appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take note of the patient's accidents, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and swelling, and numbness, and fever, and the eyes to issue forth and redden, and other similar things in more than one disposition, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no unbelievable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the skin under the bone be corrupted and the accidents that we have said come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the break of the bone comes just to the skin that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you split the split part thus: and it is that you take hold of the patient's head wounded, and uncover above the bone in all the ways you can, and above the wound as gently as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if the evacuation of blood comes to uncover the bone, or an abscess opens up, then bring forth the aid that is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with damp cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and make the wound rest until the abscess is appeased and you are assured of the evacuation of blood; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two manners of work: one manner is that you cut in a narrow strip before, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put one other cutting, larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have multiple cuttings of diverse sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron indeed; and work lightly, lest you wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you administer cuttings with tarers, not too deep lest they penetrate outside the bone of the skull, and there should be above the point a margin or a circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have more than one, so that each comes into its place from the edge of the bone, so that you have tarers for all tests; and this is the form of the three manners of tarers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one tarer on the bone and turn it to your hand as much as you know the bone is pierced; then place the tarer in another part a little bit afterwards, and do this all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the pertubations, and make it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw out the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the joint.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and cleaned the bone, it is necessary that you remove the roughness that remains from the bone to every other instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be more slender and subtler than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if there is nothing left of the small bones or scales, then remove them lightly with one of the instruments; and then treat the wound with poultices and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another manner of work is that which the Gauls say, which is more wholesome; and it is very strong, and this is their saying.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break appears most, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place underneath the head of this lenticular incisor, which has the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side only, and the part is ague on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you cut lightly all around the bone, and take good care of the skin that is underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is attached to the bone, then remove it lightly, for it is removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break of the bone does not reach to the skin, and the bone is cut so that it is only above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove that roughness, and to take away the scales with a subtle scraper which you should have in various quantities, in order to administer the most suitable thing in each place, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	So that you take away first with coarse scrapers, and then with more subtle ones, and do not cease to do so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-cutting and breaking subtleties, it is necessary to bring about a cause according to its direction; and this is not answered by he who has set his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the scab is uncovered, then it is necessary that you take one cloth of linen, according to the size of the wound, and wet it in rose oil, and put it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and wet it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so as not to trouble the scab, then minister above one other linen, and do not strain it too much except until it covers only the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it thus for one day or two days, until the abscess is pacified, then loosen it, and minister medicines such as lily roots, and vetch flour, and incense powder, and aristology, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and minister afterwards medicines without mastication.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and take care that the wound is soon clean, so you do not leave any ointment, nor allow it to assemble again, for when bowels assemble above the skin of the brain, they will corrupt and putrid, and bring great harm to the patient; for when something biting is put on the scab, it will necrotize above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no worse comes to pass except from the medicine you have put on, and that virtue has, then it is necessary that you take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and mix them with one cloth, and put it on the scab.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then complete the treatment in the ways of treatments that are necessary, until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two bones above are broken, or one against another alone, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, except it bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you insert your little finger or probe into the bone, and put this breakage into your finger's indication, and push gently by degrees, until the bone returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this lightly, and take care that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the bone, and it cannot come to its place, then it is necessary that you put it equal at the top of a rod about a foot long.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, then do it similarly, and try to restore it as much as possible on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess is pacified, then probe at the top of the bone with cloths of linen, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you probe another part on the other side, if there is a break there; and let the probes be so big that they fill the cavities of the bone.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some restorers say that the probes should be moistened in butter, and changed each day. It does not seem to me that this is well, but it is necessary that they are moistened in the concoction of almond oil, and flour powder; then leave the probe until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one probes the bone with goose feathers instead of cloths, and if there is a soft cloth around it, and the break holds, and the patient breathes through it; then do as you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscess comes to the bone while you are working on it, then put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in a little pot of aquilong.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscess does not come, then apply an ointment by degrees, made from vetch flour and incense powder, concocted with almond oil, and put it on light poultices, and do not bind the bone.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break in the bone is small and it is broken into small pieces, then bring it to suitable instruments for this purpose, then close the gap, and the cure of things that are torn apart and joined together, as with plasters and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the bone, then the cure of cloths, and put strips of linen on it, until he is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jawbone fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken below, and there is no wound ahead, and the break is above only, and is not broken in two, except for small cracks inside, then one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right side of the jawbone, that you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left side of the jawbone, then insert your index finger from the right hand, and probe the break lightly, and adjust it to the other hand by degrees, and put it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is split into two, then it is necessary that you administer an extension of two parts, until it becomes equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move or are broken, then stretch them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and put a cerate on the broken jawbone, and put a double cloth on it; and put a great well-made strap or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jawbone, and tie it as tight as you can, and tell the patient to rest, and feed him light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure is changing, then remove it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed; and put an ointment on it, made from flour powder with almond oil or vetch flour, after you have removed the cerate; and put a light linen cloth on it, and if the ointments are hardening, and the patient's disposition is not changing, leave it alone until he is healed; many times it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, then take care that no piece of bone is removed; if necessary, remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then it is widened by fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is none left, then apply the wound, if it is wide, and put on one of those plasters that are suitable for this, in order to prevent flesh, until he is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks more often in front of the shoulder, and the breakage is so according to three manners: or it is broken and separated into two, with pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a breakage with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is such when the breakage is without wound, that you should have two ministers, one of whom holds the assistant that feels the forceps broken; and the other stretches out the neck towards the part; then put the breakage in your hands, so that it forms as it should be, and there be neither appearance nor wavering.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch further, then place under the shoulder of the patient a rounded spear of cloth or linen, and make it thick according to your need; and straighten and lift the forceps, and hold the spear in your hand, so that you put the breakage in its proper place.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forceps forward because it comes out too far, then it is necessary that the patient lies somewhat on his hatred, and places under the shoulder one middle pillow, and has the ministers lower the shoulder so that the bone of the forceps is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then direct the breakage to your hands, and if you find it debris-like, then it is necessary that you cut into it; and draw out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join for any reason, then cut with one of the instruments you have; but put under the forceps this instrument, in order to guard the socket.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and resemble a spoon, and is not at all crooked, and be just as wide as it seems to be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two handles, as you see, and one be wide, and the other narrow, such as is the shape of the wound that you made when you handled the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of hot abscess, then dress the wound, and if the shape is small, or you doubt it is hot, then apply the wound with cloths and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if cold abscess comes, then soak one cloth in rose oil, and in vinegar, and in oil, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you apply powder from the mill and egg white to the bone, and put on light stoppers, and place a spear under the elbow, if you need it.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very great band of palm size wide, then put one double cloth on the stoppers and the dressing; then take a subtle steel three fingers long and wide, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage is suspended.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the steel on the breakage, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy arm, and under the sick arm; and wrap each part separately, and when you see that the bond holds the breakage properly, and you clearly see that the steel does not move above the broken bone, then reward it each day, and when the bond loosens, then restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient sit on his back, and put a small pillow under the elbow, so that it will lift the assistant high; thus, the breakage of the forceps will be alleviated by the alignment of the shoulder, or you will tie the arm to the neck, and only untie it if bad accidents do not occur, until 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then reapply the dressing if you see that it is needed, and tighten and loosen it thus, until he is restored; and she is usually restored in 28 days, and sometimes in less time for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breakage of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It often happens that the shoulder breaks or becomes separated from its place, and it is not known to be inflamed except by touch; then prepare according to the figure of the breakage, and set it right according to its natural shape, in all ways you can; then put powder of the mill with egg white on the separated piece, and light stoppers, and a double cloth on top; then place a large and subtle steel, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there is any roughness under the steel anywhere on the shoulder, use those rough spots to tie it with linen bandages, so that the steel stays in its place; and then bind it tightly with a great bandage, so that the steel does not move from its place, and check the bond each day; and every time it becomes loosened, bind it again, and put the same steel on if it gets out of place, and make the patient lie down on his side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25. And when this number is completed, then release it, and be sure, for it is not the bone that becomes loose quickly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes before and points under the key, then make sure it is secured, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breakage of the forceps to calm hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breakage of the breast
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The breast is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it breaks often at the back. And when it is broken in the middle, then it declines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks ease, and all, and by chance vomits blood, and shows the roughness on the broken bone, and it seems to be quite open.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies somewhat on their back, and places a pillow between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the ribs of both sides to your hands, and does so in all ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then applies dressings and stoppers above the subtle steel of salt or other light material, and wraps it in a cloth, and binds it to the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turns the bond back around to the back, and tightens it properly, and rewards each hour the bond, and if it loosens, then tightens it again; and if it becomes necessary to release it for corrosion or itching that comes to the skin, or pain or abscess, then hasten and release it, and remove the dressing, and addresses what has come to be done in ways of cures; then rewrap the dressing, and tighten it until they are well.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs does not occur except in large men after the back and at the top inside, and they bend only because they are flabby; and one knows this by examination of the back.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you set the break even as it should be. And then apply an ointment and strain it with a steel tool if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of ribs is declining inwardly, then the patient feels very great pain and piercing, just like pleurisy, for the bone pierces the membrane; and he will bleed at the points, vomit and spit up a great deal of blood, and this is grievous sickness, and the ancients have put great ingenuity.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the stomach, in order to push the break away from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless hot abscesses come there, if it is necessary.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us say that one should apply poultices on the place to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt whether the poultice will draw away the superfluities from the place due to the weakness of the flesh.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us say that one should cover the place with moist wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to set the flesh even around it, then be cured with the cure of pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure because of the bone which pierces the membrane, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to incise above the place on the broken ribcage, and a tool should be placed underneath to ward off the pus; and then one must cut the bone and pull it slightly, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if they are large, and cure with ointments until he is healed. And if hot abscesses come, then apply moist cloths in rose oil on top of the place; and treat the place as needed for the abscess, and be cautious above the ribcage where it should be, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes comes a break to the bone of the neck, and it bends; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will be healed or not, then take heed if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if they move and feel well when one constrains and pricks them, know that the jointure of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if care is taken.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if they will be healed or not, then take heed if the feet are softened, and if the accident is in the hands, and on top of the back there is ventosity and egestion without volition; and when one has soothed him on his stomach, there is egestion without volition. And when he is soothed on his back and he wishes to ease himself, he cannot. Know that it is mortal: if one does not labor in their cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the thing is more gentle.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply if there is hot abscess, then put oil of rose or oil of egg white on the spine, until it is pacified; then put a soothing and drying ointment on it, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not let them sleep on that part where they feel the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bones are dislocated, then it is necessary to cover with a poultice; and extract the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a seam, then cure with an ointment releasing fat, until he is healed; and if the joint of the bone is broken, which is called the "joint of the knee", if there is one dislocated bone, take your pouch from your left hand, and place it even with your other hand at your power, then apply the ointment and steel tool on top, if you need to; then pull it out, and if there are dislocated bones, do so, extract the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the breaking of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, then there is hardly any diminution at the top; and it becomes long, and declines to the backside, and comes to the patient with pain at the place, and piercing, and swelling of what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand up to it, until you are above the breakage; and know what the breakage is and its shape; and if the breakage is only at the top, then set that breakage straight, until it is in natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is of the length, or it declines inwardly, then make the patient lie on his stomach, until the restoration of that breakage becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, then apply an ointment, and place a wooden or horn tool on top, and strain the breakage so that it does not move; and fill in the place below the ribs, until the flesh is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if hot abscesses come, do not touch it, until the hot abscess is pacified, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and strain it as it should be, if there is no other bad accident; and that is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is what is between the neck and the head of the arm, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of the two manners: of which one is that you take a piece of straight wood, full of medium growth, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two pieces with two straps, and bend them upwards, and lift the patient onto a seat; then throw his broken arm onto the wood, until it comes into place, and has about halfway a curvature of wood, then bend on some heavy thing or have the attendants stretch it downwards; then place the mirror alongside the breakage, so that the breakage returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one swaddles the patient on his hatereil, and binds the hand to his neck, then commands two attendants to have one hold what is above the bridle strap in their hands, and the other hold below each link, and each stretches to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, then hold one link below the bridle strap and above the bridle strap, and each attendant stretches to their part. And if the bridle strap is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put one link halfway under the armpit, and another towards the back, under the bridle strap; and similarly if the bridle strap is on the back, then it is necessary to put one link slightly, without labor, until the bridle strap is even above its place and above the back; then put the bridle strap in place, as is necessary, and hold it, so that abscesses do not come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses do come there, then do not hold it at all for seven days, and put a soft cloth soaked in oil of roses on the bridle strap, until the abscess is appeased; then hold it, and the manner of holding it is that you put an ointment on the bridle strap, then bring the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and wrap a cloth around it, and hold on to the shoulder and on to the arm, so that the arm be in its natural position, without any hindrance or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use splints, and put on the bridle strap a larger and stronger splint than the others, with one or two spaces between each splint, and have each splint be so large that it passes the bridle strap three inches from each side; then hold on to the splints, in the manner I said at the beginning of this chapter on the bridle strap, more strongly and less moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the setting of the splints and the binding, as we said, in the case where you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is hot, then leave it tied for seven days, as we said; then look at each three days to see if there is no itching or swelling that comes to the place, or if numbness cannot come to the member because it is too tight. If this happens, do what we said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents come to pass, then do not loosen the bandage until after three days or more, and have the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and put a soft linen cloth under the armpit, and watch each hour of the day or night to see that the shape of the broken member does not move or become loosened; if it is so, then address it through the power of medicine, and give him food as we have previously mentioned, in such a manner that the food be for the subtlest substances; and when he begins to recover, let it be substantial.
