And it is customary that the armpit and leg should be rewrapped after forty days from the start; and then one must loosen and administer baths and medicines of ointments to address the place. And if the constriction is ugly and swollen, then wait a day or two before loosening.
de la brisure du bras	I apologize for not catching that earlier! It seems like this is just a heading or title for the section, indicating that the text is discussing the topic of "the breakage of the arm". If you'd like to proceed with translating the rest of the text, I'd be happy to help!
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fascicles", of which one is small, and that is the one that follows the pouch; and the other is large, and that is the one that is below, towards the little toe; sometimes only the large fascicle breaks, or the small one, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small fascicle is broken, the restoration and healing are light; and when the large one is broken, then the healing is bad, and more grievous than when both are broken together. If it is the small fascicle that is broken alone, then it needs to be slightly stretched out and put back in place.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large fascicle, then it needs to be held more firmly; and stretch it out on a cloth, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the other fingers, and the little toes lower than the other toes, so that the patient is crossed over himself, with one cloth in front of him higher than the patient does not suffer any labor; then have the attendants stretch the arm to the part below his hand, or to a link, and another attendant to another above. And then put it back into its equal shape, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break there are pieces, then put each one back into its place; and if there is none that is loose and can be pulled out, but you cannot restore it to its place, then make a splint with wood or bone, as we said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if the break has a wound, I have spoken about it in the singular chapter; then take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the restoration, hot abscesses arise, then apply a cloth made from rosed oil and white wax, which should not be too hard or too soft; and bind the cloth gently above, until the hot abscesses are appeased. And then remove the cerote, and put an ointment made with flour of the mill and egg yolk on it; then apply splints, and have the splint of the breakage be a little stronger and slightly wider than the others; and know that there should be 5-6 splints or more, depending on the position: whether the break is in one bone or two; and bind more above the break than elsewhere, and always less moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are on the break be soft and moist, not hard or dry; and let the thread with which it is bound be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And reward the member and the link after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some bad accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary that you bathe the member in hot water, until those itchings are appeased; and let the member not be too tightly wrapped or pressed. And then begin the binding again, and if the bandage is worn out and the bone is loose, and similar things, then address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take note that swelling cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then it is necessary that you loosen it a little bit, and let it be like that for some days, until the swelling comes forth, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then loosen them just up to 20 days or around that time, then tie their hands behind their back and let their necks be equal; and beware of movement and disorder, and sleep on their back; and know that this bruising is restored in 30 days or in 35, and by chance in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand.
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and in the wrists it often happens that breaks occur, and there is no other reason for it but that it pleases many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the finger of the hand is broken or bent, then it is necessary that the patient sit crossed and sit straight in front of him evenly; then place his hand on the stretched cloth, and stretch out the broken bones, and set them equal with the mirror, as long as they are well joined; and apply the poultice and bandages if abscesses do not come forth, then put a splint according to the quantity of the part; and be enveloped in one linen drap.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the breaking is on the side around the belly of the finger, then make a bundle of cloths, and instruct the patient to wrap it tightly around his broken finger; and then stretch it with a long cloth, and be the splint as soft as the flesh of the hand, and strain it, as it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the breaking is on the outside, then it is necessary that you put a splint above and another below in the finger, so that the hand be open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and stop the swelling between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the breaking comes to any of our fingers, whether it is the thumb or one of the others, such as the index finger, then set it straight, and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or tie them all together in a bundle, whichever seems better, or place a small straight splint on top, like a pouch; and take care in the restoration and disposition of hot abscesses, and treat what comes forth, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken toe.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the toe is often broken, and it can be seen clearly when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is to tie one bandage above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then stretches each of their bandages to their part evenly; and it is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the break is near the root of the toe, then one bandage should be towards the knuckle, and the other bandages below the break. And also if it is near the knee, and then place the bandages beneath the knee, and stretch down; then set the bone equal to its natural shape with both hands, as long as it is according to its figure, and then apply the poultice, and bind it, if abscesses do not come forth.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, then let it cool down and return to your work and care; the bandage is made in the same manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you envelop the break with one bandage of doubled fabric in two or three layers, and let any excess material remain; then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the ankle, and tie a long thread between the toe and the leg, beneath the knee, and let the ends of the thread come up; then turn above the leg and toe the bandage, and place splints on the break, and put one splint above the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and toe with soft cloths to keep the binding even; then begin to bind tightly three or four turns around the break; and as you go higher up the break, and less tight; then take hold of the two ends of the thread that you have tied between the leg and toe, and tie three splints above, then return down to the bottom at the head of the thread, until you come beneath the foot; and strain it so it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, unless there comes abscess or swelling or any other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, then loosen it, and address what comes forth, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that grasp, then it is necessary to wash them, if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut the flesh, and pull forward; and care for it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And at no time is the toe broken so that splints are put on it, as in the arm and shoulder; although, in this restoration made, it does not harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the toe is restored in 10 days, or a little less or more, according to the various complexities.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the swelling of the knee.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the swelling of the knee there is often a breaking, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, then it is only a slight fissure or a puncture, and has to do with all wounds, and without wound, and this is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put back together what is torn at its joints, as long as it can be assembled; then apply the poultice, and place a rounded splint if you need one, and strain it as it needs to be strained, then restore all the dispositions that we have said in other breaks, whether hot abscess or any similar thing; and put each accident in its proper place, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the breaking of the leg.
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "tibia" and the other is called "femur"; and it has all other kinds of breaks as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is equal to that of the arm, and the work is complete.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bone is broken, then turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain and it can be seen well; and turn below. Then apply extension, and set it even, and tie the splints evenly; but nonetheless, it is necessary if the break is ugly and there are many pieces that the extension be smaller and more gentle; and align according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d'une part et d'autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	of the foot does not come from breaking, but sometimes bones of the foot break and you must take care, and there is no more than a quarter in more or less conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is breaking of bones in the foot, and you see these bones mounting one upon another, then set the patient's foot on the ground, just as if they wanted to walk, and then put your foot now on their shoe, where the bones are lifted up, and press them so that they return to their places; then apply the plaster and bandages, and under the foot of the foot a small tablet at two full feet, then bind it to the foot properly, then that you have wrapped drapes around, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days are passed, then loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are some of the toes broken, then set them right again, as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then put on each broken toe a splint according to its length, and be one pace wider, then put beneath the foot that tablet which I have said, and bind it properly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then put on each toe a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one linen cloth, and bind the tablet beneath the foot; and let it be so that the tablet protrudes above the vent of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you not forget the other things that I have said about other breakages, since we have said them; and comfort each accident according to what is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone in the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's natural shape is broken, then make her sit upright, and then incline her to the part of the back, and be held by the rear; then fill the ball with cotton, and put in as much as one stone; then lift up the woman, and gently lift up the back little by little, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of the nature, and returns the bone with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for seven days or around: the breakage will be restored, and if you see, take a sheep's bladder, and tie it to the pertus with a cord, and fill the whole bladder into the nature; then blow strongly on the cord until the bladder is emptied inside: the nature will return to the breakage; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the wrist of a man or woman is broken, then set it right again as we have said for the hand; and these breakages are not hidden from him who puts his study and use into it and intends my book. For the breakage signifies in many dispositions the right path of restoration: heed this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the thigh, when it is broken, take a goose's gizzard and put it in the thigh; then wrap drapes around and leave it for three days or so around, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for him who has a breaking with a wound, whether it be great or small, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he should be healed now, and the healings which we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then apply vinegar, if you have no other remedy; and begin to restore the breakage in that same hour or day, lest suppurations do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if suppurations come, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the suppurations are calmed down, and do not touch it on the third or quarter day, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the surface uncovered, it is necessary that you set it at a slight angle with your hands, to a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable for you to set it at an equal distance with your hands, then reset it with this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight fingers long, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this reason it is necessary for the mire to take three or four, according to what he needs in each cure of breakage; and be strong and a little thick, so that it does not bend at all under compression on the member at your work, and be straight ahead, and thick from about halfway forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", therefore it is necessary that the curved fingers be placed on top of the apparent bone; and fill it once, until it returns, and be even one against the other. And if the breakage is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then it is necessary that you shape the head of the bone, so that the instruments have possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, then shape it with a suitable instrument, such as a chisel or saw, to your ability; and then remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small scrapings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. So make sure it is in its place, then soak a cloth in black stiptic wine and properly apply it; and do not put grease or any other ointment on the wound unless it has oil, lest you bring forth putrefaction and corruption; then administer poultices when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and shape the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the breakage; and many times this has been done by foolish practitioners, and they have brought upon the patient death or corruption at times; and let the straining be softer and more gentle than for other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that some evil accident may come, as we have said, and you find pain at the spot, then do not put poultices on it; but wrap around, instead of poultices, hard cloths and tie them. And when you see after one day or two days a boil forming on the wound, then remove what you have put on top with all wine, and apply healing ointment to plaques, such as tetrafarmaceutical ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you remove the splint twice a day, morning and evening, until the member is firmly set and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be aligned in such a way that the bowstring goes down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they cross over several days and it cannot be mended but returns to its bow shape, know that there are small pieces of bone, therefore you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all these dislocated pieces which bring about that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula comes to the bone, or another manner of corruption, then you must heal it, according to what is written in this chapter before. And when the bone is broken and appears on the member, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder, and other similar ones of the great members, do not pull it out, for many times death ensues, but leave it until it produces pus; by chance it may fall out after 20 days or 30, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of boils that come on the sores
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see many times after the healing of a boil, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a sad thing to see the figure of the member; and by chance the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take heed then if it is fresh: if you administer stiptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarsaparilla, acai, and similar others, in the way that you take some of these things or all together, and mix them with stiptic wine or with abundant egg white or with oil; and put it on the joint in a poultice, and bind it well, and do not loosen it for at least three days; then release it, and start another one until the swelling is gone; or you strain it onto a piece of linen well made; for the properties of linen are such that they remove all swellings from the members; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it open above, and make the superfluity apparent; or you give it to any surgeon until it is gone, and cure it as long as it remains unwell.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and remains after the member weak and subtle, this occurs for many reasons: one reason is because it was bound too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many ties, and it could not come to the natural nourishment of the member; or due to excessive inflammation; or due to very great movements, nor at its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and make their body tender, until the blood is multiplied in them; and administer baths, and give them joy and relaxation; then put poultice on the member, so that the poultice attracts to great nourishment, and the inflammation often goes away with cold water, until the nourishment comes to the member; and revive it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the crooked member after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone appears, and the shape of the member is ugly, although it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say one should break the member anew, and many foolish surgeons have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and great evils come, and by chance death ensues; however, if the swellings and tortures are fresh, then it is necessary that they be eased with hot water, or herbs that soften, such as leaves of violets, roots, and mallow, and similar things; and make a soft plaster, such as diacodium well made, and take the pulp of violets, and mix it with goose fat or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or take fatty figs, and grind them with hemp seed, and similar medicines that ease the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by constant and continuous friction with moist hands. And gentle movements should be made to the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and durified like stone, and it needs to be removed by iron, then it is necessary to cut it all the way to the bone, with a subtle and light incision; and put attention and study into the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation comes to anyone, then it is necessary immediately to put it back in place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the swelling will increase, and by chance it may be reset with pain at the joint; therefore it is not necessary to move it to the point where it is swollen: many times this brings on shame and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	However, when this happens, make the patient sicker, then leave it alone until the abscess has subsided; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then reset it slightly, and care for each member as the treatment comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jawbones are dislocated downwards, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: or they are a little moved from their place, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang down towards the chest, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so it cannot be held, nor can one close one's mouth, and envelops one's tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself in a few days.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and fully developed, then you must reset it quickly, and do not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and in such a way that the attendants hold the head of the patient, and put the mirror's pouch into one of their hands at the root of the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is from two parts; and the other two hands be free to make equal; and command the patient to relax, his jawbones, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the attendant puts it back into place, until it returns to its natural position.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the resetting is difficult, especially if both jawbones are together, then raise them with hot water and oil, until they are reset slightly; nor delay in resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset in place, and the patient's mouth closes well without any softening, then put wet cloths on top made of oil rosins and wax, and then bind it lightly with moist threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	et the patient sleeps on his back, and his legs are between two cushions, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor does he make any effort to ease himself, but takes light food, until the pains are gone, and the jawbones are loosened;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then he eats and drinks lightly, and does not trouble himself to open his mouth until the jawbone is well loosened and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be brought back to their place within an hour, and are not converted to their proper position, then fevers and usual habits come, and by chance, dissolution of the belly, and by chance, vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a deadly sign; and many times the person in whom it occurs dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the shoulder
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder cannot dislocate from the chest downward in its continuity and from the breastbone, and is dislocated sometimes forward, and it can be felt well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and stretches out his arms; then he presses the joint firmly with his palm, and it will return; then he applies the poultice and wraps it with a bandage, and holds it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the shoulder that is on the side of the back cannot dislocate; if it does not, and if it does dislocate at some time, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the poultice and wrap it with a bandage, and hold it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and thus also is brought back the shoulder of the hip when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one way is when it dislocates at the part of the armpit below; and the second way is at the part of the breastbone; and by chance it dislocates above, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inside for the nerves; and more often dislocates below towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, for they jump forward hastily; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps away, and returns away.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, it happens to some men that they suffer a blow or breaking, and the shoulder becomes swollen with a hot abscess, and thinks it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary that you examine it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it goes down towards the armpit, and makes a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest difference between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the armpit at the point where the top of the shoulder touches it, just as if it were an ox; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck, nor move with any movements.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you can find it manifestly at the point of contact.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this manner of dislocation is not to be undone when it is new, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister lifts the patient's hand up high, then puts his fingers below the armpit, and lifts the jointure forcefully up high to its place; and the minister lifts the hand, and stretches it up high, then puts it back down; so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said within three days, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and the minister should gently soothe and calm him, just like a decoction of alder, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and should administer it.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the patient should be placed on his back, and a woolen pad of equal thickness, not too soft nor too hard, should be put below the armpit; then the assistant should place their foot on the pad, and lift the top of the shoulder virtuously, and draw the patient's hand.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and another assistant should hold the patient's head, so that it does not move down; then this shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that he is reset in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and it is that you make someone who is taller than the patient to be present; and stand straight against the side, and put their shoulder below the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit up high, so that the patient hangs in the air.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another assistant should pull the patient's hand down towards their belly. And if the patient is too light, then let him hold something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it is reset in another manner: and it is that you put a long iron rod into the earth, so that the shoulder is as deep as a pistol, and not too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then be placed below the patient, but so that it has a soft cloth on top, and the patient is standing with the end of the wood; then stretch his hand down from the other side forcefully, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a rod of two arms long and three feet wide, which has the head rounded so as to fit easily into the depth below the armpit, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie a soft cloth on top of the wooden rod, so that the wood does not hurt the patient, then place it below the patient's armpit; and stretch one arm over the long rod, and tie the assistant to the rod, and hold the arm at the top of the hand, then put the arm on a shoulder of an eschillon of a wide scale, and let the hands go down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so, in whatever way it may be, then it is necessary that you put below the armpit a woolen sphere of equal thickness, then apply the poultice adorned with powder from the mill, with incense and white of egg, on all the shoulder and around, then hold it below the armpit comfortably, and turn the strap over the poultice, and wrap the hand around its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat little, until the members are comforted, for he will heal sooner; and then eat more after five days or seven, and move him; and if he is firm and not softened, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated from its place due to moisture that has come in, or for another reason, then it is necessary that you apply cauterizations at three points, as described before in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it relapses after seven days, and the joint does not hold and cannot lift its arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or relaxed; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the breast, or the shoulders, or the back, is caused by pushing and stretching with one's hands, and another type of treatment should be administered; and care for it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes swelling in the member and tardiness of movement, then instruct the patient to take baths many times until that swelling is alleviated, and returns to its natural state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the hip
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the hip is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; and it has become dislocated in all its parts, both before and behind, and the dislocation is not restored, because one can see it well and feel it well; and dislocate accordingly according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the sick hip with the healthy one, then it can be seen openly. For the joint is twisted, and cannot bend the arm, nor reach its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it as soon as apostemes begin to form there, for if apostemes began to form there, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully restored, especially when it occurs at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and brings greater pain, and perhaps death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that when it can be restored, you stretch her hand to your two hands; and her arms should be spread out, and the hands of the patient according to the hip, around, above, and below, and bind the joint together with its ligaments, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, then it returns when she doubles her hand on her hand, and binds the hip that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and know that two people should stretch the arm, and hold it steady with two people, so that it does not move at all during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double-layered cloth long and wide.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the patient has joined the joint to her hand, then anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, and bind the joint firmly until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is at the place, then put on a dry poultice with some egg white, and strain it firmly, and tie the arm to the patient's neck, and leave it for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, then reapply the poultice and the bandage, and leave it thus for several days, until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if it feels swelling after the setting of the joint, and it becomes inflamed, then bathe it and rub it gently, and press until it is relieved; or you put a sheep's fat poultice on the joint, and leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make it enter the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	and when it sweats, then gently rub the joint, and put the poultice back on, and then enter the bath; and do so two or three times, until it is healed; and if you see, then put a moist warm flaxseed with butter on top, and apply it; it will return to its natural state.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand becomes dislocated, and the return is gentle, more than other joints. Nevertheless, it is necessary to bring it back to its place hastily, in the same moment that it is dislocated, before the swelling appears or an abscess forms hotly.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the restoration is that you place the sick hand on a board, and stretch out your assistants' hands, and have them put their palm even with the appearance of the joint, and bind it until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Furthermore, it is necessary that you look to see if it is well at the place; then have the patient put the back of their hand on a board for extension and restoration.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then have the patient put their back of hand on the board, and your assistant put their hand on the appearance of the joint. If it returns now, it's good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then apply soothing poultices to calm the hot abscesses, and leave it thus without reapplying.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint remains twisted.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and nothing is wrong with the patient except that his hands are relaxed, and he cannot exert any effort at all: then know that the nerves are cut or the arteries; and there is no other remedy worse than to strain by means of cauterization in this case, and perhaps it is not worth anything.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is back in place, then put on the poultice that we have said, and strain it and leave it for five days, then release it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any swelling, then soak it in hot water, and rub it gently until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on one side, sometimes at the back of the palm or in the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then stretch the finger, and bind the dislocation to your fingers until it returns, then support the tip of the finger, and guide it towards the part where it was separated.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and leave it for two days, and then put it back in place that day; and bind the joint with a linen cloth, as we have said, and release it each day, and make it move, and bind the joint again with a linen cloth; and do this often until it is straight.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same thing if it is dislocated at the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same thing when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Loosening of the spine's vertebrae
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine's vertebra or the neck is loosened, or there are several loosened, if there is no treatment, for the patient dies quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the eliminations jump forth without will, nor can they hold it, and many times are softened any member, or both knees or two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the spine is twisted into four parts; that which twists at the back is called "humpback".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The treatment is to strengthen if the humpback has come from childhood; otherwise, there will be no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the old ways of cures by great words, where there is no great benefit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the humpback that comes forward at the chest, there is neither intelligence nor health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes straight in both sides, and one cannot cure it except by that which properly comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient should be stretched out on his face in one place even, and have someone press down under him, so he does not get hurt;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then insert one hot iron at the head on the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a cloth under the patient's armpits, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and two ministers know the cloths, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two hot irons;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the iron as we have said, and the physician put his palms on the spine firmly, until it becomes straight again.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not become straight by this treatment, then take a board three arm-lengths long and hollow out the bottom, and the patient should be on one side, and place the head of the board under the appearance, then put the middle of the board on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and put the physician's feet on the other head of the board, and press well, until it becomes straight again; and if you see, then do so with the turning stick that turns in one's hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you insert two irons at the head of the patient's arm, and on the feet two others, and have between each iron, above and below, a palm's width apart.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and have in each iron one hole, where the turning stick runs, and let the irons be firmly in the ground, so that they do not move; and between each two irons is a turning iron, above which the cloth turns, and on each of the two turning ones are two small irons a palm's width long, to turn the turning stick.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the cloth that is between the armpits to the turning stick at the head, and the other cloth to the feet at the other turning stick, and each of the ministers turns his turning stick all along the cloth, and the master puts the spine straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is straight, then place on a drying plaster with an abundance of egg white, and then bind with cloth, and then apply a poultice from a three-fingered piece of linen that will strengthen the vertebrae and the part of the spine to be healed, then tie with a cloth, as we have said, and use the patient's subtle nourishment until he is well.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if nothing comes at the end of healing, then it is necessary to administer soothing and calming medications with the poultice that we have said before; and sometimes one must administer a piece of gelly.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and sometimes there appears in the back part of the spine of the back, and one thinks it is dislocation; but it is the bone that opens, for which one should not have presumption: by chance death might come.
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder do not come from anything other than dislocation alone, nor does it come like the other joints; and the joint of the hip is loosened according to three parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more loose inside and less so in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the afflicted leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the afflicted patient's knee appears more swollen than the healthy one, and the afflicted patient cannot double his knee over the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the place that is below the swelling of an abscess hot, because the head of the knee joint comes loose.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one to whom it occurs at the front is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of the one to whom it occurs at the front is that his leg is well according to its completion; although he does not double his knee without pain, and if someone tries to make him walk, he cannot do so beforehand, and holds back his urine, and swells with anger, and when he walks, it passes above the ankle.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of the one to whom it occurs at the back is that he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the anger is softened, and the head of the knee joint is at the level below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this type of dislocation are that you strengthen if the dislocation is ancient and it remains according to its condition, if there is no cure; and it is not necessary that he have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the one whose dislocation is fresh, and it's of the three ways of dislocation, then hasten that you turn the joint, and stretch it inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; by chance it will return, and there is no need for another cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this way, then it is necessary that you appear one strong minister, and stretch the leg strongly with two hands, or with one cloth tied on the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and the other minister stretches his hand above in this manner that he puts his hands under his armpits, then tightens it with a soft cloth on the knee; and another ties the head of the cloth.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they all stretch up and down at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at one time, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to three similar things, and if the dislocation has been restored, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not, then it is necessary to apply a cure to its kind. When the dislocation is in the shoulder, you should instruct the patient to place their hand on their good side, then put the bandage on the root of the hipbone, and the part that is below the armpit, then stretch the bandage upwards towards the armpit and towards the forearm.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then take another assistant's arms, and encircle the thick part of the sick hipbone, and stretch it out far enough: if it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is more gentle than others.
